O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, very dear sons, I have completed this book for you which is the last in medical science together with its fulfillment, and I have made an end by its explanations and by its demonstrations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is greatly neglected in our region and has been deprived of everything everywhere, knowledge is lost and obscured, and only small fragments remain from ancient times in the books that have been preserved by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, intentions are obscured, and knowledge is banished.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I should revive it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I shall come along with the forms of the iron instruments for cauterization, and other tools of work with the fitting adjustment of the explanation and preparation as required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes this must surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, such that they know the judgment of limbs, their forms and conjunctions and separations, have knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of them, their movement, and of the moving vessels and resting ones, and where they emerge.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	Et for this, Hippocrates says that knowledge with the name is a lot, and with work is little; especially in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should beware, lest they err and harm people; thus I have seen many times among those who engage in this practice without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut an abscess of scrofula from the neck of a woman and cut the arteries of her neck; because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who treated a bladder stone in a man with water, and the stone was large; he took out a piece of the bladder along with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took care of the Duke of our land, who had a broken leg with an open wound. The surgeons, full of ignorance, set the break over the wound with strong ligatures, leaving no room for drainage, and left it like that for some time. They commanded him not to remove it, and so he remained until his leg became completely swollen and his foot was lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to release his leg. When I undid the bandage, he immediately felt at peace and no longer experienced any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But however the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another wound will be opened to increase the abscess, and then it will become inflamed due to the malignancy of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is purged of melancholic humour, one must not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place where all that is corrupt can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, my dear son, you must know that surgical work is divided into two categories: namely, works where there is danger in several circumstances; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is necessary for you to be cautious so that the foolish doctor does not speak ill of you. Take your weapons in confidence, approach your patients gently yet firmly, and employ the best method so that by God's grace you may achieve salvation and receive praise. Leave behind terrifying diseases with severe consequences; remove your weapons from anything that causes doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can journey from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonishments: "Do not treat any severe illness unless you want to be called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and other medical procedures involving heat, and the chapter is organized from head to toe; it also covers the shapes of instruments, the tools for cauterization, and everything else necessary for the procedure.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and using cups, treating wounds, extracting arrows, and similar procedures; and this chapter describes the instruments used in order.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar issues; it is ordered from the head to the feet, and describes the instruments required.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I explain the quality of help and harm for each humour.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest speech and subtlest science and the most secretive reply; many wise men have spoken about it and agreed on this, but their words are few as I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization universally assists all constitutions where there is substance, except two constitutions: namely the warm constitution without matter and the dry constitution without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the warm and dry constitution with matter, some argued that cauterization is greatly beneficial; while others said the opposite, that it isn't effective for illnesses arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat warm illnesses due to heat or dryness, and says he who disagrees that cauterization provides great relief for warm and dry illnesses occurring in human bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the constitution of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, only those who have tested it and who understand through long practice the chapter on cauterization, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of illness, and how conditions arise over time; we have no fear for other constitutions, especially regarding cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the surgeons agreed and concurred with the cautery method.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that the union of fire and cautery is one of the secrets of healing, and it has greater benefit than any burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth unless to the member that is cooked, and it does no harm to any other member so long as one is careful.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines travel from member to another remotely, and cause the member to fall ill with hard-to-heal diseases; and perhaps kill the patient Fire because of its loftiness and goodness of its substance does not do this, unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and the length of my service and study in this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this I apologize for the length of my words, as I do not wish to take away the secret that resides within fire, and the quality of its work, how it removes diseases from bodies, just as the philosopher said in demonstration; now receive this into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, they agreed on when the cauterizations should be performed, choosing eager volunteers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that cauterization is suitable at any time, for the harmful consequences can be mitigated by its aid; especially if the cauterizations are needed urgently to alleviate pain and prevent greater harm from befalling the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as the foolish physician does; for a disease that is healed by cauterization will not return; and they say it so; but it is not as they believe, because cauterization is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries up the humors causing pain, and is better than regular medication due to its swift action, and the strength of its effect.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is a remarkable thing that the disease may sometimes come about according to the patient's constitution and the location of the illness and its severity; these superfluities are accumulated within them due to excessive consumption of food and similar things unless cauterizations are administered where there is little excess and moisture, such as dental cauterization for pain, or similar procedures. This can resolve such pain but it occurs rarely
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	Many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cautery is valuable after medical treatments have failed, their intentions are false, and it is cautery that becomes the final treatment for such conditions because when we administer various methods of treatment for a particular illness and they fail, then we perform cauterization, which works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Thus it is clear that cauterization is the ultimate medical treatment, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with a gold instrument is more effective than with iron, and they claimed this because of the quality of gold and the purity of its substance; and they said that the color of the cautery site does not cause harm, but this is not true as I have proven it, and I have found that it is indeed true for some people; and gold cauterization is better than iron, just as they stated.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	However, when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by its color, and it may cool down quickly; and if it is overheated, it will melt in the fire; thus, there are enough drawbacks to it.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery which we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	For I have ordered this chapter of the head to feet, so that it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are used for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two types that are done due to an illness called "soda", and because of many humours that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, causing numerous dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially all illnesses that come from cold like paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a medicine that dissolves and cleanses III nights or IIII, according to what their constitution, humours and custom can bear; then let them sleep the night away.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make them sit crossed-legged between your hands, and place their hands on top of yours; after this, put the root of your palm onto the root of their nose between their two eyes; allow yourself to come close, bleed a little afterwards, heat up the cautery called 'olivare', which is shaped like this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on the spot marked with ink, and move it up and down while squeezing your hand repeatedly in a twisting motion; then lift your hand gently, look for the bone; if you see it, stop there, but if not, repeat the cautery until you do see the bone as I've instructed; afterwards take one pouch of silk, place some soft cotton inside and put this on the spot, leaving it III days; after that apply softened cotton in butter, keeping it covered until the burning sensation has passed; finally treat the wound with an ointment called 'tetrafarmacon' until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the elders said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason it heals better.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one must let the cautery burn until part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and it shall be treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one must keep the cautery in place, and press down so hard that they scrape away some of the bone, as wide as a woman's pin that is put into her gown for this reason, so that the humors may issue forth; and it should be left open for a long time; afterwards, it must be treated and sutured.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be good at all in any way, except perhaps in some people if there is a sign of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave it alone; for the shoulder becomes weakened by the continued effects of nature, as we observe this in other body parts; and even when the patient's shoulder is naturally weak, and the first type of cauterization appears more beneficial and effective to me, and thus I use it whenever there is a need.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the entire head is afflicted with chronic pain that persists for a long time, the patient must use herbs and pills called "cochie," as well as purgatives, oils, and poultices; and if one performs the cauterization we mentioned earlier, but it brings no relief.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the shoulder of the patient is of a strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize below that cautery we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, perform the cauterization on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and do a cautery in the place called the "vessel"; and there are places where cups are applied; lighten your hand so that you do not see down to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and the cauteries on the corners must be more subtle than those used for the middle part of the head, and here is how:
dou cautere dou chief	For the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in a part of the head and extends to the eye, and the skull is cleaned with softening medicines, and other treatments I have mentioned for dividing diseases are carried out, but none provide relief: then make cauterizations according to two methods, namely with hot iron and cold medicine.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with cold medicine is as follows: take a piece of elm wood and remove the bark, then cut it into two parts at both ends, after that split open the temple where the pain is felt in such a way that you can insert the elm wood under the skin; when this is done bind it tight and hold it tightly for twelve hours; afterwards untie it and press the piece of elm strongly against the wound, leaving the wound as is for two or three days; then apply cotton soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to do so, use some of the combusting medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on combusting medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is performed in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizing instrument, which has this shape.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called a "clamp" due to its head being shaped like a claw with some curvature and a small tip in the middle; place it on the painful area, hold your hand steady but slightly turn the iron so that half of the blade's edge burns; lift your hand before the artery burns, which lies outside, and an abundance of blood will flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After apply cotton in the shape of wool, and place it there for three days; then put moistened cotton with butter, and afterward cure the spot until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with a cautery called "cultellare," be careful not to cut the artery during this non-chronic migraine.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat a migraine as we have previously mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauterization methods previously described in medicine and with iron are insufficient, then you must heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it turns white; cauterize by placing it on the spot, drawing a line half an inch long, and withdraw your hand once, being careful not to cut the artery or reach the bone; be cautious of the movement of the jaw when chewing, and ensure that the patient does not move their neck nor experience spasms, and be wary of the heavy bleeding from the artery if it is cut, especially for those who are unaware and unstudied in this matter; leave the operation halfway. I will explain to you how to stop the bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where that is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on top of his head just as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you wish, apply the cauterization that we mentioned in the chapter about arterial extraction, with a cautery tool which has two blades; this type of cauterization is better than the former one and more beneficial.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain in the ears due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear arises from coldness and one must apply dissolving medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned before in the classification, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "point", of which here is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la torture de la bouche	The torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be treated by cauterization other than those caused by phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not use cautery on similar conditions arising from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this condition of torture caused by phlegm from sores and cleansings of the head, and gargling, if it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and a third where the two lips meet; apply the cautery to the part that appears healthy, and place it above the ear on the head, a little below the crown, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; leave the cautery there until half of the heart's beat has passed; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the surgical knife we described earlier, but it is slightly more delicate, and the blade must be a little thicker; treat the site as I explained before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old condition and you treat it as we have described, and there is no improvement, and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the location called "vessel" as we mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; treat them as we have said previously.
de litargie	Of lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills to clean the brain; after removing all hair from the patient's head, apply on the occipital bone the sinapi poultice which is described in the treatise of plasters; and this is how the cautery should be done: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, make three cauterizations within the head descending to the neck, with a space of two finger widths between each cautery; treat them like others, and if you wish to add more, and the patient can endure it, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others above the two horns, and treat until healed; let the cauterizations be as 'olivare', as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed of hairs and other things as we have said before; after shaving the patient's head, make a cauterization in the middle of the head and above each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient can endure it, and the illness is severe, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; let them be until the strongest part of the heart is burned, then lift your hand; treat until healed, and let the cauterizations be as 'olivare' which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cauterization unless they are phlegmatic; first, the brain must be tempered with herbs and other treatments as we have described in the section on treating severe cases where the patient is unable to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot withstand this, let him gargle and chew often to temper the brain with good meats; afterward, remove the excess phlegm from his head by pressing on it in the middle, then perform cauterization as we have described before, cauterizing both vessels and each horn. If the patient is strong but suffers, give them the same cauterizations I mentioned for those who suffer paralysis and softening of the body: along the spine and neck; let the cauterizations be of olive oil, done in the manner that has been explained.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform this subtle cautery procedure as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When melancholy is caused by excess or corrupted moistures and thick phlegm, then cauterize with several cauteries as we have described for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if melancholy is caused by excesses descending into melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will cleanse their brain, as described previously in this treatise.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Clean the patient's head; then make a linen cap well-formed, like a helmet, and place it on their head; have the patient sit cross-legged, holding still from all sides; apply a liniment, preferably made of old goat butter; heat the iron to a moderate temperature, so that the skin can bear its touch; remove the circle from inside the cap on their head, and let it cool down; perform this treatment once a week for the patient with additional good care until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you want to cauterize him by making several pricks throughout the entire cautery site.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This type of cautery softens the brain equally; then apply wet cotton on top, moistened with butter and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	from the awe (of the eyes)
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the awe (fright) first comes to the eyes due to the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something purifying for the head, protect them from all moisture, and make him sweat in the bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards instruct him to raise his head and cauterize between the eyes, making two cauteries over the two temples if the descent of awe is in both eyes together, or one if it's in only one; and avoid all veins and arteries that are below the heart when doing the cautery, which should be long according to the width of the temple; watch out for excess blood flow, and stop any bleeding you see with as much force as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will instruct you in the extraction of arteries and the incision, cautioning you on how to staunch it; sometimes a cauterisation is made below the two bones at the rear.
dou cors des larmes	the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and flow over the veins, or close to the arteries that appear outside the head; and it is seen that these are cold, phlegmatic excesses, then apply the cauterisation that I mentioned at the start of this work, descending towards the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, two on the two temples, and two below the two bones at the back; and if more is required, carefully cauterise above the eyebrow with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Through the body of tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit from it, then give the patient to drink three nights with cock's grease; after, raise his head, and cauterize him in the middle of the olive-shaped part; and make two 'clavilis' cauteries above the two wrists, a little below the hairline; and be careful of the artery so you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the 'clavilis' cautery:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called 'olive'.
de coi ci est li forme:	from which this comes to be :
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that do two cauterizations on the two thumbs as long as the nails are and leave your hand there until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes turn inwards and prick the eye, so one must perform a cauterization by two methods: with fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then place the patient on your bench; afterward, draw on the paper of the eyes a figure that is similar to the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be by the hairs; then put cotton moistened in egg white and parsley poultice on the eye, then heat the cautery with which this is formed:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize on the figure you have marked little by little many times, until the heart of the place is burnt; and the sign of the success of the work is that you see the paper retracting, and the hairs standing at the tip of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moist cotton in butter as long as the scald passes away; afterward cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs grow back and the skin is softened, then resume the cautery on that same spot as you did before; and if the hairs have fallen out, cauterize it until the skin rises to its natural place, and is even, without irritating the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cauteries of medicine are when you instruct the patient to leave the hairs intact until they are large and even, then make parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; take French soap and live heat, each in equal parts, and grind them together well; do this quickly so it doesn't cool, then spread it on the form you have made like a myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin around the eyes; if the patient's illness is only in one eye, operate on that one alone, but if both are affected too; put moist cotton wool soaked in egg white underneath the eye; the patient's head should be upright and your finger pointing upwards on the medicine, press once with the thumb and index finger each time the patient feels a burning sensation from the treatment, for they will feel as though being burned.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite has healed, lift the cloth of water, and observe if you see the paper raised just as it was previously due to the fire or incision, and if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply more medicine to the place where it has been opened before, until your work is even and your eyes are precise; then cover with cotton soaked in butter until the burning heart is cooled, after heal the wound with an ointment called "diaphenis" or another, until it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to be careful with your work, take great care that none of the medicine goes into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hairs prick in the eye, so restart the medicine on that place which is softened by the paper itself, as you have done before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and let not the right way be refused by one who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula with cautery.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not bring benefit, then it is necessary that you use cautery according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy side; hold the ministers' head between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then apply moist cotton wool soaked in egg white or parsley juice onto the eye; afterwards, heat up the cautery which is shaped like a dovetail joint, ensuring they match; if you wish, make sure its point reaches from one end to another, and similarly if you want it to resemble a tent; however, this dovetail shape works best for your procedure.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards, press the fistula if it is open and extract any pus, then dry it; if it is closed, operate on it and draw out any foul matter forcefully; afterwards, place a hot cautery iron onto the affected area, keeping your hand over the cautery near the knuckle above the eye to ensure you do not make a mistake; finally, insert the cautery into the eye socket and burn away the corrupted flesh.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you start with the cautery at the bone level, it would be beneficial.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, resume the cautery again and repeat if needed, leaving it for three days. Afterwards, apply moist cotton wool soaked in butter, and treat with a drying ointment until it is healed. If forty days pass without healing, use corrosive medicine to expose the bone; treat according to what follows in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a method of cauterising a fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Examine the fistula, then make an incision in the site. Afterwards, insert into this opening a slender probe of similar form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	et they make it to the size of a .З. of lead; and hold your hand or implement firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not run into their eye; and one must place over the patient's eye moist cotton with egg white or honey: the lead thus reaches the site of the fistula, and heals remarkably for great health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, one must administer a perforation by the nail, and return the fistula to the body of the nail according to what is needed in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	Cracks in lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur on lips which are called "hair", especially those of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as mentioned in the previous text and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it inside the cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterward, cover the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	On abscesses of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess occurs at the root of the throat or in the tonsil, palate, or tooth roots, it becomes infected and swollen and turns into a fistula; you treat it as mentioned previously, but if it doesn't heal, then you must use a cautery according to the size of the fistula; open the fistula's hole and keep your hand steady until the hot iron reaches its bottom and furthest point; do this once or twice after treating it as described earlier, until it is healed; if it heals like this, that's good; if not, you must uncover the area and remove any rotten bone according to what you find in the relevant chapter.
dou movement des dens	The movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it doesn't help, then place the patient's head on your lap; afterward, heat the cautery that will be described hereafter in such a way that you put a stick over the tooth; insert the hot cautery into it quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; after remove your hand and repeat the cautery according to your preference; then fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and keep it there for an hour and rinse well.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the moving tooth is stabilized, the softened gum restrained, and the corrupted moisture dried up.
de la dolor des dens	From the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain arises due to coldness, whether it is actual cold or not, and medical treatments are ineffective, then there is a need for cautery in two ways: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is done as follows: take cow butter and place a bit of it in an iron or copper spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a stick, dip this in boiling butter, and apply it to the aching tooth until it cools down; do this often enough for its effect to reach the root of the tooth. You can also soak wool and cotton in cold butter and place it on the sore tooth, then put hot iron over it so that the heat reaches the end of the tooth
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauterizations using fire are such that you should take a cane of iron or copper, and make it thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; afterward heat the cautery, from which its shape will come after, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cauterization is cooled down; do this often, because pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the urgency of this cauterization, and then let it cool; and that is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the upper lip's cauterization wherever you wish, and according to your ability; and that is the shape of the cane:
des scrophules	Des scrophules
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrophules are caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and they do not respond to digestion through medicine, then heat the cautery tool with what is described below, and make two openings for smoke to exit from the other side of the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, use a smaller cautery according to its size, and leave it there for three days; then apply moist cotton with butter to remove the burn; afterward, treat the area with ointments and dressings until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overwhelms the channels of the brain, especially when it arises from a cold constitution, then the patient should first be cleansed by solvents; afterwards cauterize at the root of the throat, but take care not to reach the throat itself, and burn only a little of the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, perform another cauterization at the junction of the neck and skull, with cautery called "clavicle," as described before; treat the area as mentioned earlier until it is healed.
de la toust	From the throat.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	Whenever all chest diseases are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and it is an old illness, perform two cauterizations on the vertebrae in their view; another cauterization in the middle of the breast between the two breasts; and let the cautery be called "clavicle" according to the form previously mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see fit, perform the fire cautery by pricking at all points that form what is called the "point" in ear diseases previously mentioned; and let there be thirty or so punctures around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the area as previously stated, let there be three rows of cauterization in this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauterizations are lighter, you must do three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder's dislocation:
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it is pierced through to the ribs, and four cautery marks would appear together; and for this, cauterization is done with the three-pronged cauterizer, thus forming six cautery marks; and these are the nerves according to their subtlety, and this is the shape of the three-pronged cauterizer:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	and sometimes it is adjusted to this one nerve, which results in eight cautery marks.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterward, place the powder-filled cauterizer on it; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated again soon afterward, then do a quick cauterization on the thick part of the collarbone, or many cautery marks by pricking deeply.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and excessive moisture afflict the stomach, extracting it from its natural state, and catarrh multiplies within him, and usual treatments are employed yet bring no benefit, then the patient must be reminded of his back, extending his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Next, make three cauterizations beneath the buttock with a spoon-shaped instrument as deep as a thumb, for the entire cautery is clavil. And two cauterizations outside the two sides such that the shape of the cauterizations forms three angles, and there should be enough space between them so they do not join together when cast out; and let these cauterizations be so perfect that they purify both parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauterization take this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and for one who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and bleeding on the stomach at one point according to the amount that you wish to insert; then cauterize it all over with the cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver feels pain due to cold and moisture and is burdened by excessive flatulence, such that it is thrown out of its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated according to what we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit him, then the patient must be reminded about his body; and apply three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on top of the liver, outside the hypochondrium, where the man's ribs are located; and there should be a space between each cautery equal to the thickness of a finger; and the cauteries should be as long as the body, do not press your hand too hard during the entire cautery; and only burn half of the heart, and have the patient stand upright on their feet; if they cannot, then let them lie down, extend their legs, and lift their arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your wish is so, cauterize these cutellarius cauteries (cauterization by a surgical knife), if you are skilled and wise in this art; be careful not to burn the entire heart, for it would cause all body tissues to dry up; avoid reaching the mouth, since the heart is very delicate there, as you know well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver and you need to know if it's within the liver tissue or on its membrane: If it's inside the liver, the patient will feel a pain that isn't too intense; but if it's on the membrane, they'll suffer from violent pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this treatment must be applied, the patient should be reminded of it on their head. Next, incise that place where the abscess is, and afterward heat a cutellarius cautery whose shape resembles the following drawing:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the wound until the heart is burnt, and it reaches the bone marrow, so that all redness is gone; afterwards treat it according to the cure for boils until it is healed; and no one should use this cautery other than those who have studied medicine for a long time, by whose hands these illnesses have sometimes been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then one may operate boldly, yet it seems to me that leaving [it] is better.
dou cautere de pleuresin	A ligature cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for a ligature cautery one should make roots from aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, also as thick and as long as your finger; soak [it] in oil, then put it over fire, and cauterize with a ligature cautery between the throat and neck, and two small cauteries slightly downwards on the part below the beard; two cauteries between the fifth rib and sixth, declining backwards a little; one cautery in the middle of the chest, another above the stomach, and one between both shoulders, and two at both sides of the chest outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; do not press your hand hard, but do it lightly as when anointing.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancients said that any man should use a fire cautery like a razor, heat it up and place it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess; burning away the pain as we have said with the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula develops which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of a mouse as we have said in the sections on treatments, and it does not improve, then there are three types of cautery which are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
