Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous up to those which are visible of the heart; and then do likewise in the middle incision until you reach the other side; and then extract blood equally and compress the place for the extracted blood; afterwards, put in each incision a plug made of old cotton, and cover with moistened bandages in wine, oil and honey, taking care that hot abscesses don't form there; on the third day remove the ligature and apply abundant tepid water, then treat it with basilicon ointment together with rosehip oil, and other treatments used for wounds until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	Of the disease of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a severe catarrh and you see their eyes sunken and small, their vision weakened, the membranes burnt; and hair falls out, there is pain in the head with swelling, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that this matter and such catarrhs do not arise except from many veins, and the treatment for it is as follows.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	Tell the patient to lay on his back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead and another from one side of the head to the other.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Start the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let it go down to the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that are related to eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then put old cotton and linen thread in between the two lips of the incision; next bind some cloths moistened with wine and oil on top, and beware of hot abscesses; when this is taken away, you must rub the bone until flesh starts to grow there, then treat it with drying substances that promote flesh growth.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts wheat flour and four parts colophony to make a plaster; apply it on these wounds to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	The cleaning of the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains, or insects, or mineral stones or similar metal objects; or seeds, such as beans, peas, pulses; or flowing matter like water and liquid substances and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When stones or other objects that do not fit the ear fall into it, and do not grow in the ear, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you can see the stone, apply a few drops of violet oil or oil from sisymbrium (hedge mustard) to extract it; have him sneeze with comfits, and plug his nose when sneezing occurs, then wrap around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; hold the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If she jumps from pincers, that is good; if not, use subtle extraction with small tweezers; and if it cannot be done this way, make a brass rod and insert the end of the rod into the ear canal firmly, stop up what surrounds the rod with soft wax so that air cannot enter along with the rod; then pull strongly, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take some glue that birds are caught with, put some on an instrument which is pointed to do this, wrap a bit of cotton around; press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, then pull.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out by all these things we have said, then hasten to split the ear rather than abscess becomes warm and spasm occurs; and the method of the incision is that you first bleed the patient with the cephalic vein, extracting blood according to its measure, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, incise a small slit in the root of the ear at the fatty place where it depends; and let the slit be like a crescent moon, so that you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, suck it quickly to your mouth; treat until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if this tumor is here and it swells, proceed with its extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer a very thin spatula according to the following form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and apply an incision on that tumor.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you suspect the tumor is moist due to ear moisture, until it has been cut into many pieces; then extract with subtle pincers and suck it out, as we have said, so that the extraction may be eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of water which falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to sneeze first and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she has been wounded by this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many thin and light stones according to the length of your finger, heat them slightly over a fire; place one end in the patient's ear canal and allow it to exit through their other side, then pierce the stone within the ear with another heated stone until all the fluid has evaporated so that she may be healed entirely. If you wish instead use reeds: insert one reed into an ear hole while holding its other end over fire until more than half of this burnt away; repeat process using new reeds till no more liquid remains as mentioned previously regarding stones in ears treatment.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of insects such as fleas and similar creatures if they have small bodies treat accordingly as mentioned previously for wounds; however should their size be larger so that one can feel them employ extraction by tweezers which offers a quicker means than other methods available for taking out these bugs from ears.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have mentioned in the section and chapter on distillations, and the treatment is not effective, you must then examine the ear in sunlight; if any worms are visible, remove them with fine forceps, and if none are seen, take a reed like this one:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Push the finest end into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck steadily on the entire reed; do this often until all the worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey and come out, pack cotton around the reed as I have said for stones; and if they still do not emerge as we have mentioned, apply the distillations that the ancients have tried and tested for expelling worms, which you will find in the chapter on distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear with this entire instrument, of which there is an illustration:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, and desus overs por distiller; and por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, and se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, and ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, and li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, and presse ta main tempreement tant that li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; and lou sente li malaides dedens, and soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; and garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	For the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without holes in their ears; and this same thing happens to men due to the stuffing of a wound or something stuck inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes becomes complete within the ear, so it cannot be seen; and sometimes it occurs outside the hole, and one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which becomes complete and cannot be seen is quickly cured in many ways, and for this visible one it is necessary that you put the patient's ear towards the sun; look inside: if you see any apparent inflammation, treat with all of these remedies as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and pointed in front and behind all over, so that it does not cut the ear; if the inflammation is due to something stuck or a piece of flesh within the ear, then take some subtle pincers, and gently remove it until all the matter is gone.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the scabs are complete inside the ear, take a subtle, light razor and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the ear's body.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you perceive the scab which causes the patient itching in their ear, pierce it slightly, ensuring that you do not injure the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a tent according to the size of the hole, and moisten with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, taking a tent and moistening it in rosewater, sprinkling ground vitriol over it; if you see swelling of the ear, then remove that tent and insert another one soaked in ointment composed of sweet oil and wax, continuing until the swelling is reduced; then treat them until they are cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and employ other treatments that stop the flow of blood as outlined in the section on distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of writings.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This elderberry, which comes from writings of the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must treat with tongs and forceps, and scrape off a portion of its roots with a spatula; then apply crushed vitriol to the affected area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if there is no improvement, then perform a subtle lenticular cauterization, and the cautery instrument after incision should be moved; often this requires multiple treatments, as any remaining root can regrow; when they are burned with fire, these roots are destroyed and will not return.
de la gresle	Of the hailstorm
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times on papers there are some things that appear like hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason, this disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the works [to be done] are as follows: take care if the hail changes from one side to another, and this is a light thing to know; make then a wide incision, then lightly pare the skin of each part, then take [it] with pincers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot cut without piercing the paper a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the incision is large, gather it with a suture, and treat until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointments will restore it quickly and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, it turns the eardrum upside down, and grasp the hail with a pair of forceps, and cover and press from one side to another; and if the eardrum is removed by incision, it causes no harm; and when the hail is extracted, rinse the eye with salt water, and treat the place where infectious matter breeds in flesh until the patient is cured.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that forms in the membranes of the eardrums above, and this happens more often in children than adults, causing great harm to their eyes, and they develop catarrh in the mornings, and are unable to look at the sunlight due to tears filling their eyes; because of this, they lay on their faces with their eyes closed, and sleep upwards, and their eardrums beneath their eyebrows become moist as the swelling and appearance have covered the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exit of air between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	The manner of the operation is as follows: have the patient place their head on your lap; then take a linen cloth and prepare a funnel-shaped device according to the amount of air that escapes from each part, then place it over them; press with your fingers from one side to another so that the exit of air gathers within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moist area using a sharp spatula, but do not make it larger than the wound you make when opening a vein; and cut the skin perfectly until you reach the exit of air; and in various cases, air escapes from the incision, forming like a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract it then as one piece of cloth padding between your two fingers on the outside, and turn your hand to the right and left so that it is spread out; and be careful not to get close to the gap, lest you reach all the way to the spatula near the eye, lest you injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the splinter does not come out at first in the gap, then widen the gap slightly until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then dampen the cloth with oil and water, and place it on the spot, and restrain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for such people who grind salt and place it on [the wound] to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it reaches the hot abscess place, so treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of papers.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs grow that are not natural and are neglected, they harm the eyes, causing various ailments such as customary tears, softening of the papers, and albuginea, leading to eye destruction; and the treatment is done in four ways: either with cauterization by fire or with medicine according to what was said earlier about cautery, this being done either through incision and stitching or with canes, as I shall explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head on your lap and turn their paper from the eye into your left hand; if it is turned over, that is good; but if not, you should insert a needle with thread near the margin of the paper where hairs grow close to those hairs and draw the thread over all of the paper, then shave it flat using the razor; next make an incision in the portion below the paper, underneath the unnatural hairs, carefully cutting away everything from the large lacrimal up to the small one; afterwards withdraw the thread and place beneath the paper a little tent made out of cotton and cloth, then press onto the paper with mastic, like myrtle leaf, while also making sure that the shape matches the quantity you want to lift the divided paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off what overlies the small powers equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, take a needle with a thread, and insert it into the face; and pass one end of the thread through the large cavity, and the other end through the small one, then gather the threads equally between your two hands; lift your hand evenly, and raise all the skin you have clamped upon as we have described, then join together the two lips of the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed; if an abscess appears at your incision, ease it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; sometimes it happens that the hair on the paper becomes converted: in such a case you must use what has been said about the incision; but the suture on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of gangrene is in this form: you should turn the paper and make a slit inside according to what I said; then you must make two canes per art, and two thin ties as long as the length of the paper, and with the width of the spatumile; cut at both ends of the two pieces where you hold the threads together; then assemble one and another carefully on top of the eyelet made in the paper, stretch the two canes from each side formed thus, leave it for several days, and the stretched leather will die and blacken, rot until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, you should cut with force, then treat until it is healed. Once the wound has fused shut, and the paper lifted, hair shall not grow there anymore. This is how to make two canes as shown in this figure, according to these dimensions of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, and place a delicate silk thread in it, then gather the heads and tie one to the other delicately, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread briefly into the shaft, and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient put their head on yours; and be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for it is a delicate and small work, then insert the needle throughout the shaft close to the root of the hair, and make it pierce the paper swiftly until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the shaft, and place in the shaft this hair, if there be one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out towards the whole shaft into the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Et if the scab is treated and the hair does not come off with it, you will treat the scab from beneath along the entire thread that you have placed there until the scab comes away from the hole above and you see it by sight; then you will remove the scab and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days until the hair has re-rooted in its place and flesh has grown back over it; and if the hair is small, take a single long natural hair from the eyebrow and fasten it with this one that you are leaving there so that they are extended together then remove them.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the ulcer of the eye.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or the ulcer occurs in the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And [these injuries] occur suddenly due to wounds, or cuts, or cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment is that you should split this adhesion, and separate its lips, then insert linen threads inside, binding it until it heals; and do not use anything in their care that dries out or constricts [the wound].
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do not, the illness will return worse than before; but use softening substances such as fenugreek; and boil water or other liquid with flax seed in it, and ointments of daffodil bulbs melted into any oil, and wrap a thread around this, then treat [the wound] with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the secret of your treatment is that you should take care not to let it heal in the same way as before; and these treatments we have discussed are only meant to prevent this illness from returning in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" is truly natural, or an accident.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds, cracks, cauterization and similar things; the way to work on it is as follows: take a needle with double thread, insert it into the flesh, making it pierce from left eye socket to right one so that the thread emerges in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the skin above all the way along the needle, cutting it at about 1 inch wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is required, it is good; but if not, take a razor and place it in the gap, turn over the paper and make two slits on its side; let these be at either end of the incision you have cut, making angles such that when they are joined together their shape will resemble that of an 'I' in Greek script; then remove this flesh according to how much is necessary beyond what follows the paper's edge, then join the two parted sections with a thread of woollen yarn and let it heal by means we mentioned concerning softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a crack or a suture or a cautery, you must open a full incision under the hairs of the skin, and according to what is mentioned before; then separate between the two lips of the wound, as I said; and one should perform the treatment according to the form of the illness, for it has very diverse forms, and the wise master prepares all his skill to make the figure return to its natural state; and the patient himself, depending on what is needed in terms of work and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Suddenly from the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this healing occurs in men's hands such that the skin over it is stuck to the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must put the tip of a razor under the skin and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers until you cut off what has dried out by using a subtle spatula which should not be too sharp nor blunt so that the patient does not suffer from the spatula being too sharp wounding the eye; and let your incision where you peel away this assembly be light, such that the skin returns to its natural state; and heal all of this assembly, sometimes with saltwater in the eye, and wash with clean water, and use a collar; then place between the skin and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool soaked in egg white; and after three days stop using the collar and things that dry out until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the fingernail of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the fingernail is according to two manners: it is nervous and similar to a hard surface, and another which is not nervous, but resembles frozen white moisture, when touched with iron and thought to be scraped by pincers, yet cannot; both appearances begin towards the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all vision, light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is such that the patient places their head in your lap, then opens their eyes; lift the eyelid with your hand, then coil the fingernail onto small pincers, and extend it above; then take a needle, and attach a horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and strong thread; double the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing through with the entire needle, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it above, and scrape out all the hair alongside the nail that attaches to the eyelid and the eyelashes down to the head, then remove the remainder at the root of the tear duct with an extremely thin spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh around the tear duct so that through the incision the body of tears may not come; sometimes the fingernail is extended only onto the pincers, and thread, as we have said; then scrape it out with a very fine spatule such as this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure the spatula does not touch and break through the fleshy tissue, and that the plumule is not pierced; after the incision throw into the eye a pinch of ground flax seed, and some colloidal lead, leaving it there until the next day; then treat with what is needed to heal.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the pincers cannot enter, this type of similar nail is often treated by medicine; it grows as I have described earlier in the chapter, and if you see it cut, treat the eye of the patient, and take a light spatula slightly sharp according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail carefully above it, and if you see that it does not diminish in size and the root presses against it, then drip from your mouth into the eye a mixture of colloidal lead and red ochre and ground flax seed, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same process, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as a warm abscess, then lance it and treat first the hot abscess until it is healed; then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh from the eyelash bed causes great harm to the eye, then suspend it with a hook and remove part of it but not all at once so that no moisture comes out; afterwards pour red collar ointment into the eye which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	Of flesh growing on the cornea.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men's eyes there is sometimes born red flesh which covers the cornea and grows onto the iris and turns outward, resembling a rose of pomegranate; the treatment for this is that the patient should place his head in your lap, then you open his eye, take all that flesh with suitable hooks and hold it firmly; cut away the first piece of flesh, and keep cutting with a razor until finished, being careful not to injure the eye during the procedure; make incisions using the spatula we described earlier for nail surgery and with small forceps such as are used to remove warts, as shown in this chapter's illustration; when all incision is complete and all flesh removed, fill the eye with powdered wax or pour red collar ointment and similar corrosive medicines into it, and place cotton soaked in raw egg white on top of the eye so that you may be sure abscess hot has been prevented. If any remains behind, if pus appears above your incision site and you suspect abscess hot, then ignore the eye and treat the abscess with things soothing to abscess hot; return later to your work when it is healed, thus proceeding until all such flesh on the eye shall have been cured by these means.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless, it is necessary for you to relieve the treatment of each weak eye in a natural way; and in an accidental manner, with the use of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these procedures until you see that this limb can bear the procedure.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Above the eyes are red veins that cover them, hindering their function and weakening vision over time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is thus necessary for you to first examine the eye, where it is affected, whether there are other diseases aside from this redness; then treat it in such a way: instruct the patient to place their head upon your shoulder, and then suspend those veins with a thread according to your expertise, making sure that the stitches are subtle yet firm.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And there are two ounces per degree in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully coil the forceps around those veins, wipe away the blood hour after another, until you see those veins recede from the eye; and take care not to wound the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this work at midday in front of the sun, being very diligent so that you cut only those veins; and when you have done this, instill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt that which remains from the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to gather all of this in that hour, then apply a plaster onto the eye made from things soothing eye pain, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and there is assurance of warm abscess, then resume according to this manner which comes before until it is healed; and this is the form of forceps:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon names this "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, there is pus within that you must cut over the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the instrument of which this has the form; and it is called an "aspere chief", and made of iron until the head, and pointed like a file as it is in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the wound is closed, and flesh has grown over it, and the body of the fistula is sealed, remaining so for forty days, and there are no new developments or abscesses, and no adverse symptoms occur, then know that it is healed; if not, there is another remedy to bring the fistula back to the navel opening in this manner: you must uncover the bone a second time with an iron instrument, and sharp medicines, and when uncovered take one chisel like this, which has three angles, and let its handle be tapered as shown here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the ridge, keep your hand an inch from his eye, then turn the chisel until it pierces the bone and the patient feels a breeze passing through if he holds his hand over his navel; you may then restore the opening with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and hardens at the opening, push the matter to the navel; this is an easier process for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the eye's exit
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens entirely and there is no obstruction or narrowing of the nerve, you must bind the patient; then treat it, then apply cups or hatchet without injuring to suck out, then place on the eye a poultice made of alum, aloe, incense and storax, and then strain the eye, and put ointment on bandages and cloths; and the way of the cloths is that you take quite soft cloths, and double each in four, and then put one upon another according to the amount the eye needs; then apply a firm splint above, and repeat cups to suck without hurting; then remove the cups and keep the eye strained day and night, and if the bandages soften, you must strain it strongly; then remove the bandage after day and night, and if you see the eye repairing, that is good; if not, repeat the poultice and cloths and binding and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Through the rupture of the dry membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When ruptures occur in the dry membrane, it opens up and expels papery substances like resin grains, which is frightening to see; if you notice this, the procedure is such that you insert a needle into the root of the affected area from below until it reaches above, then insert another needle with double thread from the eyelid margin; pierce through and leave the first needle in place according to its position; cut the double-threaded spot and tie a piece of membrane around it, securing it well, then withdraw the needle and apply moist wool soaked in egg white onto the eye; leave this until the threads shrink along with the membrane, then treat the eye with comforting agents until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound needs to be constrained by membrane on either side with a circular piece of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give great cause for concern, pierce them with a thin spatula that reaches deep into the eye, remove the white moisture and lower the eyelids, then insert it immediately; afterwards extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye socket
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, called "alcunnati", is nothing but the bow of the eye which is assembled in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not water; and the way of appearance of this work is that you make the patient sit on a straight chair, then take their head between your two hands, move them until you see the bow coming above your eyes; then be stuck, do not lower or uncover the light, and let the patient see things as usual; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make an incision on the horny tissue with one poke through the continuation of the conjunctiva along with the horny tissue and the cornea, until the bowels come out; and when they have emerged, pour into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then let it be cured by another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Eye waters.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similarities to eye waters in the dissection, and what is required to pierce them; so we act according to good health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light so that the sun doesn't shine on them, and bind their healthy eye tightly shut; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left, or in your right hand if they're right; then take into your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument called 'almagda', or to your left hand, if the eyes are right; then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea with the thickness of a line on that white part of the eye at the base of the lower eyelid, then push the instrument which is called 'almagda' skilfully, and turn your hand so that it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that almagda goes to the empty place; and the measure of the way almagda must be exactly of the space between the plum-stone up to the end of blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone on that paper due to the clarity of the horny tissue, and then put the instrument where there is water, then squeeze it from underneath using another way.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, the patient sees it before them and an instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, if the water rises again by another route, insert the needle with force and when it is well inserted and stops rising, remove the almugem gently while turning your hand back and forth; then put in a little gem seal agaric, and raise from this eye within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then cover the eye with outside swabs or linen moistened in rose oil and egg white, and bind it together with the sound eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on it ground cumin with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the emollient cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are such people who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called 'alberit', of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Puncture only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it a subtle incision; then put in the emollient as we have said; and upon completion of this work, provide the patient with an attractive pillow, on which they sleep on their back in a dark place; remain still from all movement, eat light foods, and refrain from moving their head either to the right or left; be bound according to his constitution for three days; then unbind him in that same dim house, test his vision, make him look at certain things, and then bind him again until the seventh day; this must not be done during the hour of treatment or after incision, but you should raise his head slightly, so that the fluids drain swiftly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess becomes hot, you must open the eye before the seventh day and treat it with a remedy for abscesses; when it is soothed, then remove the bandage from your sight and put on its face a small dressing to cover it for one day, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then take it out of the house gently and gently, and if it converts to this state; and know that no disciple should get involved in such a case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And then a man came to us from Iran who told us that in his country they make perforated almagda, through which water is sucked out, but I have never seen any such thing in our land nor read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps this is a new invention.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of alchemy, so that those who do not know them may see them; and they should be made properly of brass.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of these be made with this same subtle skill, and the last one in three angled corners.
de la char sor le neis	on top of it is a horn.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born tails of different sizes joined together, and some of these look like scorpions with many feet; and if it has a tail marked with colored stripes, and the body is soft of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case, of these tails which are soft and not marked, you must make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; open his nostrils, and take hold of those tails, and pull them hard; then cut off what you can sustain with a sharp subtle spatula on one side, until you know that tail is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be cut off, open it with all the subtle instruments gently so nothing remains; and if you are overcome by suppuration or hot abscess, treat them as required; and if these are malignant abscesses, hasten to cauterize until the blood is extinguished and all flesh removed, then pour on vinegar or sharp wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the vinegar works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not penetrate as required, know that there is new flesh on the bone above which prevents the instrument from reaching: then you must put a piece of linen thread slightly thicker than a hair into the nostril until it reaches its end, and tie two knots near each other at a distance of about an inch or less; let the patient grasp the head of the thread in his nostril with all his might, pulling gently until he draws it out through the nostril into the mouth; schools boys often do this which is easy for those who wish to perform it; then hold one end coming from the nostril with one hand and the other from the mouth with the other, and follow carefully the knots which are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this so that you know the nose has corrupted this flesh, then pull out the hair, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nostril as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all remaining flesh; then insert into the nostril a piece of lead for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is how to make an instrument to clean out the nose, with which oils and medicines are applied to the nostrils:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp, like a rod, and similarly constructed; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for cleaning out the head; and have one hand on the head to hold it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease arises on the head near the nose, which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large until it appears visible; thus, you must cut it out at its beginning, and remove all of it, then apply a cauterizing agent or burning medicine to the area; if one waits too long to treat it when it has grown large, be wary if it is hard, of dark color, and lacking sensation: one should not touch it with iron, for this is an entrenched abscess, as when it is cut once, great harm comes to the patient; but if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can be entirely removed, then empty the patient and remove it without fear, and treat the area with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the surgery involves one of these cartilaginous operations, it is rarely beneficial, except for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must therefore see to it that when it happens to someone, you examine whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; then join the two lips together with a suture, then treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side or the other, you must remove all the flesh from their hearts until they bleed, then bring the two lips together in a suture, and hold them fast, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and ground incense upon them; put over the powders a piece of strong plaster or some other sealing plaster, and leave it there until it scabs over by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you bring together the edges: either with needles, as we have mentioned in abdominal surgery; or with thread, as I have instructed you.
des apostemes des levres	An abscess of the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Malefactors often have abscesses inside the lips that are hard and resemble grains of wheat, some small and others large. In such a case, you must turn back the lip, incise each nodule with scissors, grasp it with pincers, and cut off its core in all directions until blood is drawn; then leave it alone for now, dressing the wound with powdered glass mixed with vinegar to cauterize it after the incision, until the bleeding ceases. Then let it heal easily, treating the place with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	For the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often there arises on the gums compacted flesh, which the ancients call 'albulus'; you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, letting out pus or blood; then apply ground vitriol, or other drying and astringent powders; if this flesh reappears after incision, which often happens, cut it away again and cauterize: it will not return after cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of abscesses
