Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes growths are found on the tooth roots inside the mouth between the gums: ugly, rough crusts; and sometimes teeth turn black or yellow-greenish as the decay reaches the gum, making them foul-smelling; you must seat the patient between your hands with their head in yours, and extract teeth or crusts until nothing is left; do this for blackness, greenness, yellowness and other stains so that they are cleansed; if what is causing the problem at first is not removed, begin to dig again on the second day, and the third, until everything has been dug out; know that teeth require different forms of instruments to extract them according to their condition, as the scaler used for external scaling has a different shape than that used between teeth; you must be provided with these shapes and others.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay the extraction as much as you can, for this should not be done; because it is a very high-level substance until such time as one has no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is compelled to extract, you must be certain of which tooth is causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, leading to the extraction of a good tooth; yet the pain remains because the evil root has not been removed, as we have already seen with these unfortunate people; and when you are absolutely sure which tooth is causing pain, you must scrape around the tooth with a sharp spoon to protect the gum from all sides; then use your fingers or delicate forceps for the first gentle pull and pull until it is well loosened, then clamp the forceps tightly; and have the patient's head in your lap between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it cannot be removed, take one of these instruments and gently insert it from each side, moving it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and worn down, you must fill it with small pieces of cloth where the hole is; then gently grasp it with forceps so that it does not break when extracting; and one must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, for this could cause the patient greater pain than before due to the root's cunning nature.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware not to act as the ignorant surgeons do, driven by their haste and boldness, sometimes breaking the jawbone, and failing to treat what we have described; but instead bring about severe diseases due to roots left behind or a broken jaw, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, clean the place with wine or egg white and silk; and if bleeding occurs, which is frequent, fill the space with powdered vitriol; and if this doesn't help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one extracts teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not double when you extract the tooth. These are the forms.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when extracting, and be well-made iron, and toothed in order to hold onto the teeth.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, you must place moist cotton soaked in butter over the wound for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the wound is softened, you can insert pincers which are called "algefri", and the head resembles a bird's beak. The interior should be shaped like a rasp, and this is its form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these tongs, then you must uncover all the flesh around the root and insert the instrument known as "althali", which is shaped like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out with this, it is good; but if not, assist yourself with all of these instruments, which are shaped as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need help with this instrument that has two edges, its shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other iron instruments which are in front of the reason for the teeth, and this instrument that looks like large tongs, its shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these instruments be strong so that they do not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; also other instruments which are not mentioned; wise masters find their own tools for themselves according to the work that needs doing and the illness it is needed for, because there are such diseases where no instrument was taught by the ancients due to its diversity; if a bone is broken or damaged then seek out the appropriate instruments I have told you about, which will help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be thick and well-gripping to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but can be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, take out all of these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and are ugly, especially in young women, you must know if the tooth is newly formed after another one, and it's not in its proper place, and cannot be treated or filed: then extract it; and if it is connected with the other tooth, take this instrument which has this shape, and resembles a small beak, and let it be made of iron sharpened at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And strike it several times with a hammer for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you don't move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, then use this type of file which has this shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also similar to the file used for making needles; and with this file gently shape the tooth several times, so that it doesn't move as much; then smoothen it at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, you must file its roughness until it becomes even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen due to impact or fall, and the patient cannot bite down without them falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but it is ineffective; then they must be secured with a golden wire, for silver wire turns green and decays, but gold never changes. Let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the wire and pass it doubled between two healthy teeth, then place the tooth or teeth that are loose in between them, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then restart covering up to the part where you began, drawing your hand carefully and gently so as not to move it; make sure the ligature is at the root of the tooth to prevent escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the gums of the thread with a pair of tweezers, and assemble them, and rejoin them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not injure the tongue; then leave it as tight as possible for as long as it can remain there, and if it loosens or the thread frays, tighten it with another thread; it would stay in place and serve thus for its entire duration, and this is the form of teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth, and two moved ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place gradually over time, as we have said; and do not allow anyone who is unwise or impatient to be involved, sometimes a tooth made from cow bone is used and placed where the missing tooth was, and tightened as we have described, and it will remain there for a long period.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the bond of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	in no instance is this bond found under the tongue by nature, one is born thus; or due to an accident of a healed wound; and the work involved is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament broadly, so that the tongue is released from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, and it's due to sudden wounding, insert the uncinus and cut this ligament widely; be aware that the incision should not be too deep on account of the artery below; when you've done this lift with rosewater and oil, or cold water, then place a linen strip beneath the tongue; let the patient hold their mouth thus each night to prevent healing.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding, apply powdered vitriol directly to the wound. If blood continues to escape, use the small-spotted cautery, which is suitable for this purpose. Then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it appears to be of an abnormal color, either black or hard, and the patient does not feel anything, do not touch it as this is a cancerous tumor. If it seems to turn towards whitening, and there is moisture present, scrape away the surface with an unguent, and open it from one side; if blood escapes during your treatment, apply ground vitriol until the bleeding stops then return to your work until everything is treated properly. Then clean the area with oil and silk, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses in the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils arise in the throat which are called 'godath', and properly they are known as the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and pale colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is swollen, do not touch it with iron due to blood loss; instead leave it until it matures, then you can remove it, or else it would burst on its own; and if it is white and fluid-filled, and the root is subtle, prepare your instrument for cutting, but first ensure that the abscess is warm and has calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, and his chiés soit en ton sain, and li oevre la bouche and lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, and presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; and soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, and you press the tongue against this instrument,  et tu vois l'aposteme, and you see the abscess, si pren l'oncine et lou fiche en l'amandre, then take the lancet and insert it into the almond, and traie fuer au desus plus que tu pues; pull strongly upwards as much as you can; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, and draw something from the linen with it, puis la cope a l'estrument, then fit this to the instrument, de coi ci est li forme, for this is its shape, que semble unes forces; which resembles a pair of forceps; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, yet the heads are curved, et l’un endroit l’autre, and one against the other, et sont molt agut, and they are very sharp, et est fait de fer inde ou d'andainne: and it is made from hard iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then fit it to the pincers, for this is its shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Et soit trenchans d'une part, et d'autre part nom; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, warm water and vinegar, and if there is bleeding then gargle the patient with water or boiled pomegranate rind, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood flow ceases; then leave it to heal until it is cured; and sometimes other abscesses occur in the throat aside from the two almonds, so cut these just like you would for the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed inside her throat; this is to say it was a small abscess; and it almost entirely blocked the entire throat such that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was closed off, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if left like this for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high up that two rods had been inserted through the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened immediately, and inserted a probe into one [nostril], then the probe was pushed further, and a large portion of bowel was extracted; then I reinserted it through the other nostril opening, and the patient's mouth was opened and their tongue pressed down; after that, I placed the probe in the abscesses, and cut off a part, and only a small amount of blood came out; thus, the passage to the throat of the woman was cleared, and she began now to drink water and then wine, without ceasing to drain from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, filling up the space I had emptied, until it became very large; then I incised it and cauterized inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left that place, not knowing what God would do after me.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is beneath, thick, and round, it is called an "eye.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cleansed as we have said in the division, and the cure is not beneficial, and you see that the abscesses are eased, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and for one that is round, assembled but not long, and is bloody or of false colour or black, you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have described, regarding its whiteness and length, that you seat the patient facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned before; then insert the needle into the eye, draw it out from beneath, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for incising the testicles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut away any more flesh than the superfluous part that lies beyond the natural limit; for if you remove more, it will damage the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use an instrument for cauterization to ease their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is sharp fire.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And have the patient put their head in your lap, and then press their tongue with an instrument like the one we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and sear it with hot sharp fire, not too thick nor too thin; and this is how the instrument should be shaped...
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calmly wormwood, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile and similar herbs, and mix all of them together into one pot with oil, boil the mixture slowly. The pot should be well glazed with strong clay and have one instrument with a pointed end made specifically for this purpose placed inside it in the middle:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or copper and have one end inserted into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the nose until the eye is withered; then repeat this often until the eye dries up, making sure you do not perform this procedure at the beginning of a hot abscess as many things can happen. It should only be performed in the absence of heat from an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a piece of egg shell inside the patient's mouth so that it does not become too hot; for the egg shell will not allow the steam to harm the mouth, and this is a good treatment along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often there is something caught in the throat, like a bone or fishbone or any object; therefore, you must remove what you can see, and press the patient's tongue towards the sun with all your might so that the object moves; and for what does not appear to you and remains stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit until the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps then the object will be expelled through vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel orange peel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then have them swallow it; when it reaches the right place, it will become unstuck, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, take an instrument made of lead in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be bent at the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and keep the patient's head elevated; beware not to touch the epiglottis lest it swells up, nor push any bones inwards; it is better for the patient to insert the instrument himself because he knows where the problem is; if you must do this yourself, guide the tool carefully downwards or pull it back gently until all instruments are level and nothing is blocking them.
de la sansue de la gorge	From the mucus of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never has mucus been medicine, as I said in the division of cures; and when it does not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient with the sun, after you have pressed their tongue with an instrument as previously described.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, draw it out with a very small hook, or use delicate tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a plucked hair, and push it into the patient's throat; then insert at its end a hot iron, and repeat this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient should keep holding water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the patient's mouth, pouring it in so that they swallow it, and move their hand frequently as you do this; as soon as the leech senses the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall out as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the treatment of an eye disease; do this many times, for it will surely fall.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot with visible coals, and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, where the head of the instrument should be placed; then add your fumigant, and have the patient place the end of the cane in their mouth, closing their mouth so that smoke does not escape but rather reaches their tonsils; and now the tonsils will descend, if they do not, recommence fumigation several times; let the patient suffer thirst, eating salty things only, drinking no water; then it shall be necessary for them to expel them through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat tonsils is such that when they can be seen, it resembles bent pliers for entering the throat; and has a resemblance to the beak of a bird, with roughness like a file, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; see its form here:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what the following text recalls from various sources in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; They fall into two categories: one is based on its appearance itself, and the other due to moisture content.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second category refers to their location within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the anus, and abscesses in fleshy places differ from those that occur in joints, with each requiring specific treatment when acting upon them.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if you should not pierce abscesses while the boil is soft according to its maturity; but for those that must be pierced when ripe and do not become soft with maturation, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints, and they are left to rot around it, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which is why this causes contractions in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the main limb, and you delay perforating it until it dies, this will harm the main limb; when it is near the foundation, pierce it before it dies; you must not puncture an abscess formed without digestion being complete, except for one that is near the foundation, which can rot completely, elongate inside, and become a fistula; it cannot heal quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the opening for perforation of a dead abscess according to its development, and that is when the pain subsides, and the fevers depart, and the reduction in pain and redness, and of swelling and sharpness at the head of the abscess, and other signs; you must make the perforation where it depends on the place of the abscess, and where it appears mobile; the perforation should be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there are no folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the fleshy part, it is better that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed to be fully digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the poison would be elongated, and it is full of much filth; and by chance, the lips and depth of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And for any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring small abscesses, small holes; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for those abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the heart, as when it has become like a rag and is dead, then you must do as with boils: and there are some that split into three angles, and others that are removed like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses from ants; and there are those in which one makes a round incision, other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the spirit falters with the release of bowels, which may cause the patient's death, and you will not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and once you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound clean, and examine if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a full-size lesion, insert tented linen or old cotton threads; but for large abscesses that are highly porous, you must pack each pore with a tent so that they press upon one another; and when you have cut through part of the skin to access the abscess, and turned back its edges, then fill this space with old cotton or dry shreds of linen without moisture, bind it tight for three days; then remove these dressings, cleaning and anointing until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, apply cold and light pressure, dampen some cloth, and place it on the bleeding site multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply a compress and healing salve, along with the powders I mentioned on various pages in this book. If it is winter, and the skin or abscess is very sensitive, you should place warm tents and cloths soaked in wine and oil over it; but if it is summer, and the skin is fleshy, use cold water, oil, wine, and oil-soaked cloths as described before for three days; then remove the compress, dry and treat the wound as necessary until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this you must know universally about the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with treating abscesses, and here is the chapter for it.
des soros	scars
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head of the chief comes abscesses, small and resembling webs, like a hen's egg, and many such things exist.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture like pus; and of such kind which are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you prove with every instrument which is called an "entromissoire", from whence its form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if moisture is present, they do it above the bone.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, thoroughly scrape away without leaving anything the skin that contains this moisture, for it returns if nothing is left behind; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, apply it to the wound, and leave it there until the next day; during which what remains of the night will pass.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then repeat the cotton application, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know for sure that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to it, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds onto fatty tissue, remove it in this way: from above the bone; cut off your pincers, and scrape away all around, focusing entirely on extracting the root where it lies; but if an artery opposes you, do as I have told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for an abscess if it is pus-filled, and to cut and clean as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the pus-filled abscess and moisture is lighter, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if for some of these abscesses or sores where there is no moisture, and I recall one abscess on the head of an old woman; I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if any had struck it with a tool, they would have caused just as much damage as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	With other abscesses coming on the head, especially those that appear on children's heads and at the roots of ears, make sure to open them as low as possible so that the pus may drain out; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	Some ulcers
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur on the neck and underarm, and in other areas of the body, and they are very common and linked to one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	Each ulcer is properly within its own layer, like the brain and abscess of the head, as we have said; there are many types of these ulcers.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those which you see a good condition to touch, and are similar in color to the body, and soft on all sides without being aerial like the nerves of the neck or arteries, and it is not deep; you must cut it from above, and strip off its skin on each side, and spread out the two lips of the wound with pincers if necessary, as we have said for abscesses of the head; draw it apart piece by piece, being sure that you do not cut any nerve or vein, nor should your spatula be sharp so the flesh does not escape, and take care not to go too far forward lest you cut what you must not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not stop working, apply ground glass or some blood-clotting powders to the wound; compress the wound and let it be until the abscess subsides, the wound softens, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Once the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until it is completed; then examine with your index finger if any small knots remain, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large wound in the root of the knot, do not cut that knot at its root but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall by itself without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, seeing that there remains no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must proceed to cut out the root of it, and draw out the sinews, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofulous sores that have excess matter, pierce it where the sore dies out; and pierce like the one mentioned before, depending on how it is, then apply ointment with tents and similar things, so that what remains of the corruption is corrupted; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat with an ointment that promotes flesh until it heals.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the surgery to the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is a record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with dislocation, it is necessary that the cleft of the throat, which is called the epiglottis, be examined; and no aid should be given by this means, because all the veins and passages of the patient are affected by abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the passage of the airway, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we split it below three circles or four with a small transverse incision between the two circles or according to the quantity of the incisional line of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from above.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat entirely along its length, then split the heart until you reach the windpipe; and remove the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the syfac as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the flow of air in the windpipe which must pass through the broken place, and by the defect in the voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since strangulation was suspected, gather the two lips of the wound from the heart, and cut them entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and breathing fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, make an incision on the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus avoiding death; and for this, the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the malignancy of the disease has passed, which takes three or four days. Then they would instruct to close the wound and treat it until it is healed; I will tell you what I witnessed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young lady take a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; I was called to treat her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood flowing from it; I knew she had not cut a vein or damaged her throat, and breath was escaping through the injury.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed; all that remained for the young lady was a hoarse voice, and she later returned to her normal state; from this I conclude there is no fear in cutting through the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess with a yellow color, and it occurs more often in women; it can be caused by two factors: natural or accidental, where there is no underlying disease.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	The accidental occurrence is of two types, one resembling our fat tissue, and the other similar to an abscess caused by a ruptured artery; there is fear involved, and cauterization with fire should not be attempted except in small cases, and this must be proven and examined thoroughly: if you find it similar to our fatty tissue, and it cannot open into any vein, then cut it as we cut a boil, and remove its entire covering membrane if present; treat it promptly and cure it appropriately until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	de us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways we have, of which I will speak about all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I tell you all the differences between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that they are troubled with heat and fever until the ebullitions have passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the colour of the body, and begins like a spot, and becomes large; and they are of two types, either hard or moist, and very different in colour as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You must, when you come to treat the neck, first examine and assess all the instruments known as 'entromissoire', according to their form described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire about new abscesses is that you take hold of the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the entromissoire, taking care not to spill.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture is short and regardless of its color, treat it as I have said for other abscesses; if after withdrawing the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, so make a cross-shaped incision and take hold with forceps, lightly peeling off each side and taking care of the coat where it lies so you can pull it healthy with the neck; and if you cannot pull it whole and healthy, then pull it in pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the nerve will return many times; and if a piece is left behind, and the blood irritates you, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, tighten the wound, and place soothing warm poultices over the abscess, curing it with other treatments until it heals; and if the nerve is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with something that encourages flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the beating vein opposes you or causes trouble, hasten and apply crushed vitriol to the place, leaving it there for two or three days until the wound rots, resting the boiling of the blood; then return to cut away that which remains of the night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the shapes of the instruments to be inserted, and there are three types: large, medium, and small; and among them are three squares called "albaret", and one called a "breb", and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, for probing abscesses and fistulas; and they are like needles used to sew up sores, made of brass, iron, or silver, but those that are yellow are better, and more proven is black lead for probing the crookedness of fistulas; and these come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of incisions are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are incisions with two curves in three ways; and there are incisions with three curves, also in three ways; and there are incisions with two curves, and incisions with one curve only, also in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these have what one makes them for are sharp, and there are some that only cut flesh from one side, which one peels off the nerves, so as not to damage the vein or the nerve; and of these introducer ones there are the blunt probes in many sizes, so that the patient does not feel it during the opening of an abscess; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one should only use them on fleshy areas such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling bark from a fistula, according to this form, with which one stops the bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed back into its original position to heal through the closure of veins, arteries, and sometimes according to this large framework:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, making them appear like female breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and for those who wish to treat it, one must follow this method from point b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	scorch the fat, and fill the wound with a meat-based medicine, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching them shut, treat it until it is healed; if the breast sags downwards, having become softened due to its size like in women, you must cut it into two parts above with two similar incisions; so that one part holds onto the other at each end, such that the larger line contains the smaller according to this diagram from b to g; then peel away the skin which is between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, as well as any other necessary treatments until it is healed; if it has not yet healed or the incision was not completely made due either to the patient's unwillingness to rest or else due to a loss of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton saturated in corrosive ointment, leaving this in place until it reduces the remaining flesh and fat; treat it as before so that it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are like hard scrofulae, some with sides and some containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bowels within the abscess are emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all of the cotton, and treat it gently until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofula, then treat it as we have said for scrofulae incisions; and if the wound contains bowels, apply the cautery as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	From the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is sealed, abscesses often form, and the vein also becomes swollen and infected; you know this by the fact that when it's due to the artery, the abscess runs lengthwise through it; and when you feel it with your fingers, you sense constriction; but if it's the vein, the swelling spreads outwardly; it is madness to cut open this abscess, especially where it lies beneath the armpit or neck, or in many other places, as it would be too extensive.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must therefore avoid iron treatment, and likewise with the one at the head, you should also avoid it; in the case of an artery swollen from a cut through the skin lengthwise; then make an incision with an lancet, and separate the artery carefully from its membrane until it is exposed; then insert beneath it a needle, and pierce it all the way to the other side, binding the artery with double thread at two places, as I have taught you in the treatment of the two arteries found on the temples; then lance the space between the two bindings with an introital dilator until blood flows out from within, and open up the abscess; then apply a cure that stimulates suppuration, so that the bond falls off; then treat what remains appropriately, until it is healed; if the abscess stems from the incision of the vein, you must hold in your hand as much of it as you can along with the skin, then insert the needle beneath the place you are holding by hand, and pierce it, and attach a double thread so that you draw it out to the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with bindings on either side of two parts of the thread; if you fear the thread will fall off, reinsert another needle along the full length of the abscess beneath all the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads at four places; then lance the abscess so that superfluities flow out, then cut away the excess from the heart, leaving what is bound; afterward apply a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then bring treatments with tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	From abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses form on nerves when they are injured or due to excessive work, and similar causes.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	They occur more often in shoulders and arms and anywhere there are joints, and these are serious abscesses with a colour similar to that of the body, and it causes pain in various positions; when pressure is applied, the patient feels pain, but it is not at the surface but beneath the heart. It moves in all directions, neither forward nor backward, below or above, and one that forms on joints should not be cut with an iron instrument - this could cause contraction; while one forming on the head or forehead requires the application of a spatula.
