Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has not pierced a nerve is when there is no foam on the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and they sigh deeply and desire cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the chest's covering, it is near the small ribs; it causes great pain and a great shock, and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, it may expel from the wound some undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly and no feces come out through the lower intestine, there is no hope for a cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows outward, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, like the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and loin and thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are secure according to many positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell on his clavicle at the root of the neck: I grasped it and drew it out from below the ear fat, and he was quickly healed.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out an arrow that had lodged in the fat of the eye below the paper beneath, and the arrow was bent, and he could only reach its point towards the shaft, and this arrow was as big as a Turkish bow, all made of light iron without ears; the wound healed, and no evil accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and this arrow was Arabic with ears; I cauterized the whiskers, and handled it carefully until I extracted it, and the Christian healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man's belly that had gone right through and thought he would die; then after thirty days his condition still hadn't changed; so I cut into the arrow, drew it out, and he suffered no evil accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow stuck in his back or shoulder, and the wound has healed over it, and the arrow remains inside without changing its natural position or causing any harm to his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man with an arrow in his face, and the wound has healed over it, remaining without causing much pain or other significant issues.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And extract an arrow from the king's man which was lodged in his nose, slightly angled towards the right side; and the arrow was bent. I was called to treat him three days after it happened.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found that the wound was very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I sought it everywhere with great care, but I did not feel anything; he felt pricking and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead. I applied a drawing and digesting poultice to the place, so that the flesh would not swell; and there appeared the flesh of the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on for several days, and the wound healed quickly, but the patient remained ill for a long time until he felt the arrowhead one day inside his nose; that's what he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it opened, and I examined it; I felt that the arrowhead was becoming exposed in this place. Then I widened the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine so much that the shaft of the arrowhead became visible; it took almost four months before it emerged. And then I expanded the wound further to allow me to insert some forceps, and I pushed from one side and another, but they could not get a grip on it. Then I did not cease trying different methods and tools until eventually one day I was able to grasp the arrowhead with some well-made forceps, according to the method described at the end of this chapter; I withdrew the arrowhead and closed up the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The surgeon judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	And I have told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you focus your care on what I do not mention, because books cannot cover everything; but wise masters gather much from little, and for what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in response to the strange occurrences that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows exit the body in two ways: either by the path they entered or through another opening; and those that leave through their point of entry, are arrows lodged in fleshy tissue, which sometimes happens.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't leap now, leave it until the flesh around is rotten and the outlet is loosened; and also if it's stuck in the bone and can't come out, leave it there for some days, moving it each day; then it will jump, and if it doesn't jump, pierce all around with a very thin needle until the tissue around is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the brains ventricles, and any of the accidents I've mentioned appear in the patient: don't pull it out, but leave it there until after a few days, for if the arrow comes close to the surface, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck entirely in the bone, and it does not penetrate the skin surface, and the patient remains free of adverse symptoms for a few days, then proceed to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded in the bone and cannot be pulled out easily, then administer small incisions around as I have told you; afterward, treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the arrow is embedded within the body and cannot be seen from outside, explore all possible directions to find it; if you can feel it, then extract it with an appropriate instrument; but if the tightness of the wound and depth of the arrow prevent extraction without damaging bone or nerves or veins, then widen the wound by cutting until it is large enough. Extract the arrow if feasible, and if there are barbs on the arrow that hold it in place, remove the tissue attached to two sides of the barb so you can reach it with your instrument, then break or bend the barbs until you can extract it; do this carefully to avoid breaking the arrow as this would make extraction even more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the surrounding tissues are rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood opposes you, so bring about what we have said regarding the treatment in its chapter; and be wary of incising a nerve or opening a vein, and use any means necessary to pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, forcefully or gently; and place the patient according to the position they were in when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest aid there can be, and if you cannot, so place it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	An arrow that comes out from another part, where nothing appears of it, or the skin is swollen in this area if one sees or feels anything evidently: cut above until tongs can grasp it, and then pull it out; it should come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then rotate your hand circularly until it enters the bone and widens the bone, after which pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be extracted, then leave it there for now and attempt the extraction again until it comes out; if the arrowhead is inside, push it through the entire shaft; if the head has fallen off but you wish to administer pushing, introduce a tapered tool so that the point of the arrow enters the taper of the tool; then proceed with the pushing, and if the arrow is tapered, insert a tool in the same way with its point facing inward to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around it if possible and then treat the wound appropriately.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the foot or thigh or in the belly or bladder or in the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, then do so; be careful not to cut a vein or nerve, and then extract it, and suture the wound as needed; treat until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows resembles that of a bird's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the driving wedge is like that of a bird's feather, used to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown here in this illustration:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the pincers to push and to pull is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins in the body from which one can bleed, of which sixteen are in the head: two veins that run behind the ears, called "herbech"; and two arteries that appear in the temples; and two veins located on the lower eyelids, known as "aspires"; and a vein in the middle of the forehead; and another at the top of the nose; and two veins that are on the neck; and two veins below the upper lip, which are called "augeherich"; and finally, two more beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, which runs along the left side and is known by laypeople as "the head vein"; the middle one is called "faste," a combination of the cephalic and basilic veins, referred to by laypeople as "the heart vein"; the basilic vein lies on the right side and is called by laypeople "the stomach vein", it sits over the fossa, and this is the one that appears most evidently at the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and has two tributaries; in the leg and foot are three veins: one is beneath the curvature of the left-side pocket, and the second sphenoid which is at the right ankle bone; and the vein called "nesse", which is located at the other side's ankle. There are also three veins below these in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are located behind the ears aids in treating chronic colds and migraines; and the quality of bloodletting, as I have told you, is such that you raise the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then strap the patient's neck with a tourniquet so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places of the head: seek them out with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, there cut; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein until it reaches the bone, then lift your hand up along the whole length of the vein, and cut both skin and vein quite through two fingers' breadth, and let out blood until you wish to stop; then release and bind (it), until they are healed. And I have already described incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is effective for an old and persistent migraine, as well as chronic ophthalmia, and for the body of acute tears in the eyes; the qualities of the bleed are such as I say: it must be done with the patient holding his neck rigidly so that the two veins show clearly; feel their pulses under your fingers, then bleed above this; then raise the heart high over the vein by resting your index finger on top, insert the lancet underneath and lift up the vein, cutting it like you have done to the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; release the patient, put your finger upon the wound for an hour, and then cotton wool on top of that; next bind it firmly and leave it until it is healed; we have already spoken about its incision and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient ailments of the face, and for migraines, and redness; and its quality is such that the patient must strain their neck by twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called a "fosseur", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the point of the instrument over the vein and press it down with your hand or something else, and let out blood according to the quantity you desire; then release the patient's collar, and bind the wound until it is healed and do not apply a wide flame at any time.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame must not be too sharp; and do not bleed across [the wound], as the bone is close by, and it may break the instrument if it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The draining of the two veins that are in the two temples aids the eyes, and for tinea, redness, and swelling in the eye, and diseases of the face; the quality of their drainage is such that the patient must twist his neck while being held tight by someone else as before; then drain them, and let the incision be across, a little above the length of the flame, a little wide because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, they might break; then let it bleed until you have enough blood, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The draining of the vein in the nose is beneficial for fever, sudden severe headache, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, especially when it is chronic; the quality of the drainage is as follows: have the patient twist his neck, then grab your left hand's nose, take a thin long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space between the two nostrils because the vein does not open very well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; do not go too deep, and let it bleed according to your need, then bind it for one night, as it heals quickly; this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The draining of two pints of blood helps with the narrowing of the windpipe, and at the beginning of a hernia, and for many illnesses, pleurisy, gallstones, herpes, and tumors; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient stretches his neck underneath from one side to another, as we have said; and let the master stand over the head of the patient, and let the patient sit on a chair, then open the vein of the arm widely for a short time, then draw off blood in moderation, or as much as is necessary; then do likewise on the other arm, then undo the bandage, and press firmly around the veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and let him remain like this until morning, until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The draining of blood from the veins of the upper lip helps with glue in the mouth, and with the decay of gums, and cracks on lips, as well as sores and inflammation around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of bloodletting is to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right upper lip and the other on the left, which are known for being dark and having small black veins around them: so cut both, and if you don't know or doubt it, cut the thicker one from each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, as they are of the same kind.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleeding the veins beneath the tongue aids after bleeding from the temporal vein, and it is for narrowing of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and illnesses of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeder should be such that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and they lift their tongue, and look underneath on each side a black vein: so bleed one and then the other, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by making an incision with a rather wide flame-martinated knife, or with an olivewood subtle one as sharp as you like, and this is called "anesil"; they are broad and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame marten is highly renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the swollen veins full of thick blood, and containing troubled thick blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointedly subtle, and it is for bleeding thin veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids illnesses that are below the throat, and near the neck, and under the armpit, and in the abdomen; and it is important for the bleeder to bleed carefully, and avoid the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it pierces the artery, and a flow of blood occurs, then it must be staunched, as I have said; and the flame should not be pressed upon, but cut like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, then you must extract it and change to another one; or take a segment of it, or heal in its place the vein within the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with a lancet as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of the wound, then it is necessary that you stretch out the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark this spot with a sign, then bind the arm, and cut into the vein with a lancet as we have said; watch over it so you do not strike the artery when you see the place swell up, for that is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: therefore hurry and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind his arm, and leave it thus, and let not the patient move; and be in fear, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and you faint, and no medical practitioner is present, then cut the artery where it appears, for this will stop the blood flow; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig bark, split it in two and take one half, binding it well until the next day; if the bleeding has stopped, that is good; if not, then treat him as we have said, with powders to stop blood flow; and this method of stopping bleeding is not dangerous in many situations due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The draining of the vein in the middle helps draw blood from both the head above and the body below, as it is composed of both the basilica and cephalica veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must take care not to pierce too deeply near the nerve that lies beneath, for if they hit the nerve and cause swelling, the patient will be grievously harmed, and may even fail to heal; this nerve is often visible but due to its subtlety sometimes remains unseen in some people, so you should drain it with a thin instrument; avoid piercing the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is an open wound between the two nerves, then make a long incision.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The draining of the cephalica vein is helpful as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; you should drain using an olive oil flame or a myrtle flame cautery, for this is the safest method among all wounds, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest position and not cause any harm if one fails at first, and they can start again; sometimes, some people's joints may swell when this happens for the first time, but that does not matter much.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not performed for any other purpose but to maintain health and prevent future illnesses; this bleeding can be done in one of the three veins which are known as cephalic, median, and basilic; the bleeding must take place at the beginning of Lent while fasting, and during autumn and winter after eating when signs of fullness appear; it should ideally take place on the first or third day, a couple of hours or up to three days later.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no specific time, but rather when the need arises, day or night, at all hours and in any season; and it is not advisable to bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a child before the fourth month up to seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They should not bleed the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to bleed themselves, in whatever manner, they should first cleanse their intestines with a light enema, if there is an excess of feces retained, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines harmful superfluities that would be detrimental to the principal members; nor should you bleed one who is over-sated with meat, or drunk, until such time as they are sober again, nor those suffering from dropsy; and beware bleeding after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive intercourse for women, hard work, lack of sleep, fasting, and any other exertion either physical or mental; then thin the humors if the blood is thick due to meat consumption and drinking and by medicines, if you have them at your disposal; then take a bath, should nothing hinder this, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein on the inner side of the elbow as we have said before; and guard against exertion, strain, lust, and suchlike that day; be calm and happy, and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and let him rub the arm twice or three times with his hands, then tighten the ligature moderately, for if it is too tight or narrow, blood cannot flow through it; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell up and are felt; then moisten the bleeder's flame with a bit of old oil, then put your left thumb on that vein below the place where you wish to bleed so as not to allow the vein to escape or break when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that leak like cords to the wound drain, and some are full of windiness, so that when one places a flame upon it, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein; thus it is with these [veins]; if one opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for this reason, the wound-draining surgeons must be mindful in such cases.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the wound opens up the first time, it is good; if not, try again a little below that spot or above until you find a suitable place, if the spots are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the spots are swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days, do not bind the arm: perhaps hot abscesses will appear; do not enter the bath, then restart the wound-draining procedure if you wish; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows out subtly, and you doubt that it won't drain as much blood as you want, direct all of your flame straight onto that same opening; work a little above instead, unless the spots are swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not restart the surgery, and apply a poultice of oil, for it alleviates the body from blood, and is friendly to this place the poultice that has oil; and thus administer the poultice of oil in each surgery that you treat the veins, to stanch the flow of blood; and the same does triacle and bowels when placed on the place; very subtly it draws out and separates the blood if it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs there, which happens many times, especially when it has not been operated on before except for that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and apply to the place a sponge moistened with warm water and salt, and compress it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood flow from the wound ceases, and if it remains at the place after some days any blackness or greenness, then it does not harm; and if you see it, apply something of aloe or myrrh mixed with gallium juice, mastic, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance in the wound of the basilica: therefore place your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft upon compression with your hand, then that is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore make sure you do not put anything on it from what we have said before, for perhaps the cut is too close to the artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the spot, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out blood from each person according to the quantity of their strength, and according to the colour of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see that it is thick, leave it be until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is full and robust, requiring bloodletting, that you make a larger wound for him, with wide flames; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and you should bleed them little but often, and you must do so by cutting across, not piercing; this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one whose body requires bleeding, give them bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are hot-tempered, take three or four times out of blood; and if they have a cold complexion, let them eat moistened bread with musky syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the treatment, after the loss of a great deal of blood, it is necessary that he drinks meat broth, and subtle aromatic syrup, and uses other things we have mentioned in the section on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to open his arm and bleed it again, when he is weakened by excessive bleeding, it is necessary that he bleeds little by little, according to the amount of his remaining strength, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wishes to open his arm again after the first bleeding, and he has a strong constitution, then he should bleed seven hours after the initial bleeding or after nine hours have passed since the first one.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wishes to bleed in another place, it must be done on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has much blood within his body that is already heated, and causes fever; it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the opening until it ceases in proportion; then, when you attend all conditions of healing, place your hand on his pulse as he heals, lest death come into the place of proportion, and this happens many times when healers are negligent; and it is not fitting that when you wish to unbind the arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, you press forcefully upon it; nor if it is crooked, should he extend his arm hastily, for this would be harmful; but leave it until it heals a second time; or, prick at the end of the vein so that the congealed blood flows out from the wound, and apply some wet flaxen cloth, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not restrain it until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then do so from the same place or from another vein in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arms is used for bleeding instead of the one on the head because it is easily accessible.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of bleeding is as follows: the patient immerses their hand in warm water until the nails turn red; they are then tied loosely so that the vein becomes prominent, and bled from across its width rather than length; the opening should be wide, with the bleeding occurring close to the wrist joint; if blood does not come out, immerse the hand again in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; for those who are cold-blooded, do not re-immerse the hand in warm water as this is done more often during winter than summer; bleeding from this vein is safer than any other veins because it does not contain arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bloodletting of the right hand's vein is effective for all liver ailments: take hold of the hand and immerse it in warm water until the vein swells if it can be seen; and if the bleeding occurs transversely and you cut straight across, there will be no harm; do not go too deep, as the nerves are directly beneath completely bare of flesh; then return the hand to warm water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot exit.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as needed, apply oil and flaxseed to the wound to seal the incision, and do likewise with each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bloodletting of the left hand's vein is beneficial for disorders of the spleen, and perform everything just as I told you regarding the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bleeding of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all ailments that are below the waist, such as diseases of the uterus, retention of urine, kidney disease, thigh and leg pain, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its bloodletting is that the patient soaks their foot in hot water, rubs over the vein until it breaks, and binds it above the ankle joint; this vein is located at the ankle, extending up towards the kidney; bleed from whichever kidney is closer or from the ankle as you see fit.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed from the foot, beware of the nerves below it and cut across them as well; let the blood flow freely without stopping.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot escape, then put the foot back into the water, and let it thoroughly drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision fails the first time, then make a second one slightly above it, for the location is salty; do not be concerned about nerves, as we have said, and treat the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle bone, and its incision is beneficial for relieving hip pain when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The quality of this incision is such that the patient must enter the bath, and then stretch above the ankle for four days by twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, treat the wound in every way you can, and with crossed legs; it is better to cut than to drain, as the location is salty, and it is very responsive to manual treatment.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then squeeze any vein that appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and be careful to avoid nerves; make sure blood flows freely until you see it, then release the binding, apply cotton, and compress; she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	bloodletting using cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping instruments are made of horn, or brass, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: either by wounding and drawing out blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping method without wounding is done in two ways: either with full heat or without heat; and the cupping that involves wounding and blood extraction is performed at fourteen places on the body, of which one is entirely on the head; another is at the nape of the neck; others are on both sides of the neck; the cup below the chin; those on both shoulders; those over the hips; those in both arms; those on both legs; and cups for ankles. And this type of cupping draws out only a small amount of blood, just from the minute veins scattered across the flesh, so you will not weaken anyone by it as with vein bloodletting. It must never be administered either heated or unheated to any illness that comes about through overabundance until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to the necessity of illness it is required to ventose [a form of cupping therapy], or for familiarization, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and in between and all times; because there are those who when they need to be ventosed have a heavy head; and some find fullness and redness on their face, and on their head, neck, and darkening around the eyes; and others find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, coughing up blood; and still others experience dreams, seeing through the night blood, bruises, death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially when it is in the middle of the month, we instruct to be ventosed after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with the itching of the head ... that affects the eyes, and it should not be done after evacuating all the body's blood; this venesection takes the place of bleeding from the head, and it is not suitable for those of a cold constitution or who have catarrh, as it does them great harm; therefore, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold ailments in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed in this way become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little further down due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Bleeding in the middle of the neck takes the place of bleeding from the head and from the basilic vein, and for this reason it is useful for narrowing of the throat, ruptures in the diaphragm, coughs, and fullness; it should not be applied with too much force because if it holds tightly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach/heart pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation at the two ribs of the neck is useful for headaches, eye inflammation, migraines, choking sensations, and toothache pain; it replaces bloodletting from the basilica vein; you should instruct the surgeon to press their hand lightly so they don't sever an artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Ventilation below the chin is useful for mouth diseases, gum inflammation and similar ailments that affect the mouth, it replaces bloodletting from both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation of the shoulders is useful for diseases caused by heat and excess moisture.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Ventilation of the armpits is just as effective as the three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large vessels; instruct the surgeon not to press too deeply, since this area lacks muscle and contains nerves and arteries beneath it.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is placed on the buttocks is useful for treating hemorrhoids and diseases below [the waist], and it must be large, made of brass, so as to have a strong pull; and perhaps if it were thin, it would break; and it creates big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Suction cups placed on the legs visibly drain blood from the entire body and are useful for treating old pains in the kidneys, uterus, and bladder, and help heal abscesses; they can be placed at the two hips or two ankles, but over time their use weakens the body and causes fainting in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: first place it on an empty area and apply it quickly, press down firmly, move evenly, and do not stop until you see the skin reddening and swelling up, indicating that blood has been drawn from deeper layers; then remove the cups, being mindful of individual bodily constitutions since some have dense tissue while others are more porous: thus one must strike only once and create wide but shallow wounds; suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very dense, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out little by little, we are content with only one blow.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw out a lot of blood, we start again often; and if the blood is dense, strike perfectly, and let it end so that the heart is suddenly pierced, and for those with thick and hard skin, and who have narrow veins, you must grease the cups' openings with an aperitif and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, violet oil, almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, cress oil, lily oil, chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess [matter] is large and cold, take almond oil or balm oil, aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied; instead, it should be washed after ventilation with rose water, cold water, morelle water, cucumber water, porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excessive moisture, apply myrtle water or sumac water, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those with large excess matter, use old wine or suet water, aniseed decoction or chamomile infusion, and similar remedies; one should not be bled with cupping before a bath nor while in the bath, but after the bath by one or two hours; one must remain awake after cupping and must not sleep during the treatment.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch out if the patient is choleric and has too much sharp and inflamed blood; they should take cold things like pomegranates and endive and lettuce in moderation, and similar foods; and eat little pork, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for those with a cold constitution, give them syrup of honey and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little pork and mutton, and small birds like pigeons; and on the day they are cupped, they should drink more than eat; sometimes you must give some men treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping to strengthen their principal members; be subtle with the blood, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups which are applied without causing injury are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, podagra, on the belly, hips, and kidneys, for these members do not tolerate wounding at all; we only employ them to draw blood from member to member, just as we place them on breasts when a child is nursing; to remove the viscosity which accumulates in the member, such as applying cups to the abdomen and hip to diminish the member; and it removes pain, where there is obstruction or stones, possibly by its attractive virtue removing the obstruction, or ridding the stone of its location; thus does it act also when placed on the liver and spleen when there are retained flatulencies, and these cups should be applied empty in order only to suck; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and some filled with tepid water, such as in diseases of pleurisy, and in that way one fills the cup with warm water alone or with water where suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of applying the cupping glass with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It has two inches of width and half a palm in depth, and on its side, towards the middle, it has a small hole like that for inserting a needle, and let it be made of brass so as not to hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and at its centre there is an iron or brass bar across which a candle wick can be inserted, and there are large and small ones according to the illnesses and ages of those who take them; because cupping glasses for children are different from those for old people, and those for thin people from those for fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	One must thus insert this cupping glass onto the limb: take a candle of wax or a wick soaked in oil and place it across the bar inside the cupping glass such that the flame is at the bottom of the cup so as not to burn the patient; then put the cup on the limb, with your two fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, you can let out some vapour, and remove the cupping glass; take the wick as before and relight it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass that is applied in pleurisy, for all acute cases, there is no pipe or opening, and it is only used when full of water, being placed solely on top of the affected limb; its form is as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	They are only applied to limbs where cupping cannot be used due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; also on parts devoid of flesh, like the tongue or nose, and other similar ones; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches which are in clear clean water without mud, take them out; place them one night in pure water until they become familiarized and have nothing inside their bodies; then bleed with a lancet and cupping glass, afterwards rub the limb red-raw, and put on the leeches; and when they are full, and drop off, if this is where you can apply a cupping glass, do so because it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the place of injury slightly, then with water, very well, and then press it; if the wound heals too close to the body after this, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it until the blood is stopped; and if the blood flow increases, put powdered vitriol or galls and similar things on it, until it stops; or you can place half of some peeled broad beans over the injury, leaving them there to dry out at the wound, which will now stop bleeding; and should more be needed, take additional compresses.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the compresses cannot be applied, rub the place of injury with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until some blood comes out, and then apply the compresses; as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry out; and when you see them getting wet again, sprinkle on some powder of aloes and ground psyllium, or ash, and they shall now cease.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the resetting of fractures and dislocations.
