Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish surgeon who ignores this chapter will never see any of the ancient medical books, nor read their letters; and for this reason, knowledge is lacking in our land, for I have never found a good one; and I know nothing else except through the science of these ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge from them, as well as through experience and the practice of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained within it, and have summarized it at the end, clearly showing the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the summary of the words and chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and remains on the truth so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When fracture or dislocation or torsion or rupture occurs in someone, you must hasten to bleed the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, or old age; or if the weather is too hot or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is, cold porridge, goat meat, and sheep's flesh, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill up too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a warm abscess, or an outflow of matter from the member; then the patient returns to his first usual diet.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed meats that cause quick growth, or something viscous, such as wheat boiled in water, and rice, and eggs, and feet, and cow stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For if quick growth is taken away, healing and the breaking of bones occur more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the elderly and those decrepit cannot be well healed or fused according to their nature due to the dryness of their members; nor can those who are too young, such as small children; but they will heal, apply on either side of the break large splints which bind and join the member together, so that it is strengthened like before; do not remove them from this work at all, and for this reason you must nourish them with rich meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the spine, or a leg bone, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	As there are fractures that require traction, and others by sharpening, like the slit of a quill to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is fracture with wound, or a complete fracture with slight crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type there is its own instrument and tool in the restoration process, according to how it remembers its place; and the fracture of bone can be identified by the twist in its line, clearly evident from the outside, and resonating when pressed with hand; and where there is no twisting or resonance on touch, and patient feels little pain, then perhaps there is no fracture; but could be a twist, crack or slight break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You shouldn't move it by hand; instead, apply the following medicines listed below and then hold [the shoulder] now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Know that a fracture which goes around the entire bone, and where the two parts are disjoined, they must now be brought back into alignment equally, lest hot abscesses form there; and if hot abscesses come, leave it alone for one day until the abscess has healed over; then bring it into position as closely as you can without causing pain or damage and know that its recovery will be easier than that of one where pieces are missing; hold [the bone] as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces broken in the bone, stretch it out across two supports, whether that be hand or foot, or with both hands if a small limb is involved, or with two cords, or one cord and your hands; put the member back into its natural position so that when the parts of the broken member have been brought together, bring all add-ons into their places as closely as you can without causing pain or damage and take care not to cause injury or pain through your work; and align well the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well with his hand if it seems to you that it is not well: so treat it gently, and do not strain or press it too much, for such actions cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb, as we have seen many times before.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, caution the patient well to not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, or during any other movement; and ensure that the limb is secure so that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they feel no pain, it is not yet in place, and you must put it in such a position that they feel no pain; and be careful that it is set straight, so that no crookedness comes when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs differ in their size, length, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar: one must wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and for those that are large, like thighs and legs: one must wrap them with a wide and strong bandage, for the wide bands embrace the whole of the large limb, and constrict it evenly from all sides, so that there is no pressure; then bind with light rolls of gauze, three or four turns according to the size of the limb, and tighten your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, allowing the fracture to separate a little; and loosen the bandage bit by bit, until you take up most of the healthy part, then take another bandage, and wrap it again over the broken area; then return to the part below the fracture, and bind moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first binding above; then place between the bandages rolls of linen or cloths until they are all even, then tie everything with a strip above, and finally put on your splints well-made, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is inflammation or an abscess, apply soothing ointment for abscesses that is hot and reduces swelling, leaving it there for a few days; then strap on your stars, and let them be made from half of a wide cane cut lengthwise, or from the wood used to make shingles, or from palm ribs, and let them be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the star placed over the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others; it must also be as long as is suitable for the size of the limb; then strap tightly onto the stars, just like you did with the first bandage, then bind on top with an appropriate thread, like in the first binding for the fracture; make sure it is tighter above and looser below; the thread should not be too thick nor too thin, but rather medium thickness, and made of soft flax; because if the threads are thick, as I have seen the work of fools who use coarse linen cords for their bindings, this is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and make sure there should not be more than two fingerbreadths between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the head of the shoulder after being immobilized in a cast, place pads made of linen or woolen gauze beneath it to prevent injury.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And remember, it is not advisable to immobilize the shoulder immediately after a fracture of any limb on the same day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, one should not apply a cast until five or seven days have passed, or more depending on your assessment of the level of inflammation present; and here you will find an ancient method of poultices to treat fractures, dislocations, and sprains: take flour that sits against the millstone wall, mix it with abundant egg, and apply this mixture, neither too runny nor too thick, using it as follows, which is a common way to treat fractures in various positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Autre maniere d'emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Autre maniere d'emplaustre que vaut a torsion: take mullein and marshmallow root, each 10 units; myrrh and aloe, each 9 units; acacia bark, 6 units; Armenian bole, 10 units; grind well, and mix with water or egg white, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new wool, boil it in ash water and oil, then apply to the injured area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly alleviating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves and earth-pine leaves, grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of poultice for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vetch, of each one part; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is hot, mix with moist coriander water or plain water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of stronger poultice than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mallow, and flax seeds, pomegranate rind, melilot, and sanicle, with flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; grind and mix with salted water, or fresh water, or wine, depending on the warmth of the limb and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except for ointment made of wax and oil, and no other thing more, he says this must be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen believes that one should apply to a broken limb, for restoration, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped human hair, or feathers of a bird, and viscum, and equal amounts of each, grind them together and make a plaster and bind it in place.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you remove the binding a little while later and check if the patient feels no pain nor has there been any movement of the bone from its place, do not loosen it too soon by hand. And if pain comes to this spot or itching, restlessness, or swelling appears then hurry up and take off the plaster now; grab light fabric like silk, and a sponge moistened with sea water, dip in some warm water and apply at the site of discomfort until any itchiness ceases and there is relief from pain. Then let it rest for an hour afterwards, put dry cloth on it soaked in water or rose oil, and wrap up gently each night until you are sure there is no abscess. And reduce inflammation around the limb, easing away any pain then restart gentle binding and a small amount of plaster, without tightening as much as before; do this gently until it has healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has ceased to suppurate and turned red, causes pain and is swollen, take away all of it, and then apply an ointment and bandage; repeat this as often as necessary just as before in the same manner.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If none of what we have mentioned works for the limb, then do not dislocate it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it alone for twenty days, depending on what you see, until the fracture heals, and the flesh approaches the bone; then restrain it more than before, and thicken its flesh as I said earlier; and if you see that the place is drying up too much, know that nourishment cannot come there anymore; therefore bathe it in warm water every time you dislocate it, and do this every three days, loosening the bandage slightly; by doing so, nourishment returns to the limb, and improves what the foolish doctors do, who restore the limb crookedly: this is bad, and such operations are fearful, and I see nothing else but to leave it be and work on it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	The diverse ways of breakage.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures and various forms, and their causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by the strike of a sword, and the blow removes all the bone up to the marrow that lies beneath the bone, just as an axe or a pole does; and thus this type of fracture is called 'axing'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called 'absolute'; and the wound from these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow or splitting from the impact of a stone, or falling on stone, or other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing fracture that reaches close to the membrane underneath the bone or upon it, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that pierces the bone as subtly as a hair and has a small fracture which is why this break is called "capillary", and if the wound is made by striking with stone or falling or similar, causing a piece of the bone to fall inwards leaving a gap like that made by blacksmiths when they strike pots; so does the bone go inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those with moist bones like children's heads and occurs with all these types of fractures where small fragments are torn apart like stars, I will speak about them when the time comes.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of fractures through their dislocation, and examination by touch, and the corrupted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known for this reason: when the bone is exposed and one rubs it, the black fracture becomes visible.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the fracture, take heed of the patient's accidents and illnesses; if you see any ill accident such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, fainting, a fever that comes in waves, their eyes turn red and bulge, or other similar things across several dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no terrible accidents and expect recovery, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the membrane beneath the bone become corrupt, and the accidents we have spoken of occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane covering the brain, you must split the affected part in this way: take hold of the wounded person's head and uncover over the bone in every possible manner, especially above the shape of the wound; should bleeding occur upon uncovering the bone or a hot abscess develop, then apply the necessary treatment, filling its place with lint moistened in rose oil; let the wound rest until the hot abscess has cooled down and you are sure there is no further bleeding. Then proceed to remove around the bone by either of two methods: one method being that you cut narrowly in front - which will be the shape..
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is to have several different blades, some narrow and others wide, all with points, made of thin iron; use them gently so you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and solid, you must drill around it rather than using blades with awls because they cannot fully penetrate the skull bone. The tip of the awl should have a margin or circle to prevent over-penetration; you will need several of these so that each fits into its place on the type of bone, ensuring you have awls for all parts of the skull; this is what the three types of awl are used for:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities to pierce around the broken bone are that you place I tarere on the bone, and turn your fingers until you know the bone is pierced; then move the tarere elsewhere a little after, and do so all around, then cut with the incisor knives the space of the bone between the openings, doing this as finely and lightly as you can, as we have said, until you extract the bone by hand or with any of the instruments such as pincers; make sure not to touch the brain or the meninges.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you use an awl to remove any leftover bits of bone with all other instruments similar to an incisor knife, but they must be more slender and finer than the other knives; if there remains anything from small bones or scales, remove them lightly with some instruments; then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer; he praises it strongly, and this is his saying:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first expose a part of the bone, where the fracture is visible, so that when you have uncovered this area, you will place beneath it the head of this lens-shaped cutter; here is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, as the cutting edge has two sides, so that the sharp edges face towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet above it, so that you lightly chip away at the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane beneath; if it is attached to the bone, remove it slightly, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the membrane, and the bone is merely cut above it, with small pieces present, you must smooth over this roughness, and remove the scales using a fine scraper of varying sizes which you should possess, to accommodate each place with what is most suitable, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Place large scrapers before it, followed by finer ones, and do not cease until it is well-done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other fine scalping and delicate fractures, you must provide a reason according to its direction; this is something that cannot be fully explained by one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackening occurs only due to the medicine applied, with such a powerful effect, you must take some honey and three parts of rose oil, mix them together, and apply this mixture as a dressing; then treat it in the manner of cures that is appropriate until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the clavicle are broken or just one of them, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, it does not break but only dislocates or twists, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must reach your little finger into the space where the clavicle sits and place this broken part equal to your index finger inside and push from below until the clavicle regains its natural shape; do this gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain because of your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the nose and cannot be reached by hand, it must be set level with the head of a slightly thicker nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, do likewise and hasten to reset it on the first day if you can; otherwise, after seven or ten days, when the hot abscess has cooled down, then use fine linen bandages at the head of the nose for a fracture that is not complete.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	In another place you use other bandages if there is a fracture there; these bandages should be so thick that they fill the cavities of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	Some doctors claim that bandages should be moistened with butter and changed daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened in a preparation of egg white and flour powder; then leave the tent so that the bone hardens and the cartilage becomes stiff.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are placed instead of tents, and if you have soft cloth, wrap it around, and hold the breakage, and let the patient blow through it; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess forms in the nose while you are working on it, apply a plaster or cotton moistened with rose oil, or a piece of diascordon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not form, apply a plaster from the outside made of ground flax seeds and incense powder mixed with egg white, then place light tow on it, but do not tie up the nose; and if the breakage in the nose is small, and it breaks into tiny pieces, extract them with suitable instruments for this purpose, then clean out the wound, cure it with things that join flesh together, soldering it like plasters and ointments appropriate for such a case; and if there is no injury inside the nose, treat it with tents, placing thin canes until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the breaking of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken from below, and there is no external wound, with the fracture being only outside, not splitting into two, nor bending inward; one knows it easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if it is on the left jawbone, insert your right-hand index finger and push the fracture in slightly, and fix it from outside with your other hand, making it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is split into two pieces, you must apply extension to both parts until it is levelled.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement or fracture of teeth occurs, tie them with a thread made of gold, silver, or silk; then apply cerote on the broken jawbone, and place double cloth over it; put over the cloth a large well-made starched pad or an equal piece of leather that is long and wide according to the jawbone, and bind it as tightly as you can manage. Instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you notice a change in the shape of the jaw, untie it after three days, and then reset what has shifted; apply an ointment made from flour with egg or sesame oil over it, after removing the cerote (bandage); put a light linen cloth over the ointment. If the dressing dries out but the patient's condition does not change, leave it until healed. Healing often occurs in three weeks' time.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a warm abscess forms, apply what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture with an accompanying wound, remove any broken pieces of bone; do so carefully using appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once you have removed all the broken pieces and there are no remaining fragments, clean the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable dressings to promote flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	Of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks multiple times in front towards the shoulder and does so in three ways: either it breaks into two separated pieces which is the easiest to repair; or there are fragments; or it involves both fracture and wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is such when there is a fracture without a wound, you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the fracture; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then align the fracture with your hands, so that its form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor conclusion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and make it thick according to your needs; stretch and lift the fracture, and press the sphere with your hand, so that you align the break as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the fracture outwards, because it is too close to the surface, then the patient must often lie on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under their shoulder; the assistants push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then attend to the fracture with your hands, and if you find it broken, you must split it further; draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, break it using one of the cutting instruments you have; but put pressure on the forceps underneath, to prevent necrosis.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it should resemble a spoon, and is not very sharp, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two heads, as you see, with one being wider, and the other narrower, just like the rupture of the wound that you made when drawing out the bones; and once you are sure of a hot abscess, cauterize the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you suspect a hot abscess, pack the wound with cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a warm abscess arises, soak a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, then place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Bind the bone when it is wounded and fractured by applying an ointment of mill powder and egg white on top; add light swabs, place a soft wood stick beneath the armpit if needed, then take a very wide bandage one palm in width, place doubled cloth over the swab, smear on ointment, then take a thin rod three fingers broad and long and wrap it inside that bandaged fabric so its end hangs down; insert the rod into the fracture and roll up the bandage around the neck, under both armpits – unhealthy and healthy - gently tighten until you see the splint stabilizes the bone. Check often whether the ties are tight enough to keep the splint in place over the broken bone. Reward the patient each day, retighten whenever ties loosen; make them lie on their back with a small pillow beneath the armpit at night so that the shoulder is elevated above heart level – this eases any strain on the brachial plexus by aligning the shoulder or tie arm to neck until day twenty without unbinding unless some bad incident occurs, then redo the ointment if you see it's necessary and restrain again for as long as recovery takes; most heal in twenty-eight days but for some less.
de la brisure de l’espaule	For shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Until the shoulder is healed or put back in place, do not touch it; adjust it according to the shape of the break and restore it according to its natural form as best you can; then apply fine flour with egg white and light compresses on top and cover with a double cloth; then fix a broad bandage of soft linen over this, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there is any hair under the bandage use lint swabs so that the bandage lies evenly; and bind it tightly all around with a large bandage so that the splint does not shift from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it up again, and adjust the splint if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or 25. When this number of days has been completed, remove the bandage and take care to avoid any further displacement since bones do not heal lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts forward and pierces below the heart, make an incision above it, remove it, and do as we have said for treating a broken rib to cool the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the spine
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The spine is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks outward.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downward and the patient feels great pain, lacks movement, coughs, and may even vomit blood; the ends of the bone are exposed through the skin, which can be easily felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration process involves having the patient lie frequently on their back, and placing a cushion between their shoulders; then pressing the shoulders together while bringing the ribs of both sides closer with your hands in order to align the bones correctly. Afterwards, apply poultices and cover them with fine salt or some other light substance like a bandage that you wrap around the broken bone so it cannot move; tie this roundly at the back and fasten tightly but not too much, undoing it every hour and tightening again if necessary; especially if loosening is required due to corrosion, itching of the wound, pain, or abscess - in which case be quick about it. Remove the poultice and clean the area using appropriate treatments before reapplying a new one until healing occurs.
de la brisure des costes	Of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Knows that rib fractures only occur in the back part of the ribs, towards the spine and head, and they do not bend because they are thin and fragile; one feels it well upon examination by touch.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a plaster cast, and restrain with a splint if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib fracture is inwardly displaced, the patient feels great pain, and pricking, like a prickle, because the bone pierces the flesh; they also have difficulty breathing, cough up blood clots, and it can be fatal if not treated quickly. The elderly often suffer greatly from this injury.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And so there are those who say one must administer foods that swell the belly to push the rupture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not cause this, for hot abscesses arrive there if they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, then treat them with cautery.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say to apply cups to the site to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; nonetheless, there is doubt that the cup may attract superfluities to the location due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say to cover the site with moist wool soaked in hot oil, and apply tents between the ribs to equalize the tension around it, then be cured by treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone pressing against the skin, and there is doubt in their case, then one must cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument beneath to protect the soft parts; and then one should cut into the bone, and extract gently, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess forms, place moist rags soaked in rose oil on the site, and apply it to the area; treat the location according to what is needed for an abscess, and let it rest frequently on its side where it should be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Of the broken neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes fracture occurs to the bones of the neck, and thus it bends; likewise with the backbone.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, observe if their hands become soft, swollen, and lifeless, unable to move or extend, and when you prick them with a needle, they feel no pain.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many situations, and if they react and feel well when you squeeze and prick them, know that the bone joints are saved, and the patient will recover if treated properly.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar happens to the backbone, and you want to know their recovery chances, observe if their feet are weakened, and if there is any injury in the hands or on the back, along with windiness and involuntary defecation; when they are turned onto their stomach, it should also cause involuntary defecation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is reminded of it on his back and wants to get up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal; do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not befall him, then the matter is more slight.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	The cure for it is that you apply a warm oil, either rose oil or new olive oil, until the area cools down; then place on one of the drying and strengthening poultices, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep upon that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is severed, you must cut above the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment that promotes flesh growth until it heals; and if the vertebrae are broken, which are called the "vertebrae of the neck", place your fist from your left hand against them, and make it equal to the other hand with your strength, then apply poultice and splint as needed; then hold it in place, and if there is a severed bone, do so above, remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the broken bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Before the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, there will be a little loss at the head; and it makes sounds along its length, and bends downwards, and comes to the patient pain in the place, and tenderness, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above it, so that you are over the break; and know where the break is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, make this break even, so that it has a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is along its length, or it bends inwards, then make the patient lie on their belly, so that the restoration of this break can be seen by you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it equal, apply the plaster on top, then place a piece of wood or heartwood above it, and secure the fracture so that it does not move; support the area below the ribs until the ligament is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess forms there, do not touch it until the hot abscess has cooled down, and apply what we have previously mentioned; then return to the restoration process, securing it as required, provided no adverse event occurs; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of the two methods. The first method involves taking a piece of wood of suitable thickness in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two straps, and pull them upwards, then place the patient on a seat. Next, throw their broken arm onto the wood until it reaches the elbow, and put in a piece of curved wood beneath; then pull something heavy or have the ministers push downwards. Finally, the doctors align the fracture to match the hands together so that the bone sets as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method involves laying the patient on their back and tying their hand to their neck; then command two ministers, one to hold what is above the fracture with their hands, and the other beneath all the straps, stretching each part outwards.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then bind the rope below the break and above it, and extend each of the assistants to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, then you must put a rope in the middle below the acromion, and another towards the blade, beneath the break; also, if the break is towards the blade, it is necessary to place a ligature slightly, without effort, until the broken part is level with its place, and on the blade; then make the fracture equal, as it should be, and bind it, unless an abscess appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess appears, do not bind it for seven days, and place upon it a moist lint with easy oil and rose petals, until the abscess is pacified; then bind it, and the way to bind it is that you put plaster on the fracture, then bring together the arm on the support, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and apply a bandage, binding over the support and over the arm, so that the arm remains in place without moving, unless something hinders this, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint over the fracture, leaving two inches of space between each one; let each splint be large enough to pass three inches beyond the break on either side; then draw it up tightly onto the splints as I have said at the beginning of this chapter regarding fractures, more strongly but less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of splints and their tightening, as we have said when restoring a broken limb, and you suspect hot abscess formation, leave it bandaged until the seventh day, as we have mentioned; then check every three days to ensure that no itching or swelling develops in the area, or that circulation is not compromised by being too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents occur, one must not release the limb until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with hands over stomach; place under the injured area an even wool-filled cushion, and check every hour day or night that position of broken limb does not change nor relax its bindings; if the treatment succeeds through medicinal virtue, give them food we mentioned earlier in such a way that at first this nourishment is subtle; and as they recover let it be coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the splint and leg should be removed after forty days in total, at which point one must undo it and administer bath with medicinal ointments to realign its place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and tight, it takes one day or two months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	On l'a bien remise en place. Mais si le malade est resté longtemps dans cet état, il faut la remettre en place, et alors on ne saurait trop dire combien de jours ou de mois cela prendra. Car il y a des gens qui ont les os très durs, d'autres très mous; l'un mettra plus de temps que l'autre.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the 'duo foscil', one small, which follows the wrist, the other large, which is below towards the little finger; perhaps only the larger breaks, or the smaller, or perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bone is broken, its restoration is light, and its healing; when the large one breaks, healing is difficult and more serious than if they both break together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that is broken, you should lightly extend it a little, and set it evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, you should bind it more tightly; extend it on a cushion, and hold the wrist of the hand higher than the other, with the little finger lower than the others, and have the patient cross their arms over themselves, with the cushion in front of them at a higher level so they do not exert any effort; then the assistants should stretch their arm to the part below the patient's hand or elbow, while another assistant holds the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place the mirror evenly according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, place each one in its correct position, and if there is any that cannot be restored to its place as it grips the heart, then leave it and remove it, just as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with a broken wound I have spoken about it in the singular chapter, so take care of its treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the healing warm abscesses appear, so glue I cloth made from rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth above subtly, until the warm abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the wax, and apply the plaster of the mill powder with an abundance of egg, then place the stars, and let the star closest to the fracture be slightly stronger, and a little wider than the others; and know that there must be six stars or arms in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and bind more firmly above the fracture than elsewhere, always less so as you move away, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths which are on top of the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be made from linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And after a few days, treat the limb and its connection.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident occurs in the limb, such as itching which comes to the limb, you must wash the limb with warm water until the itching is soothed; and let the limb rest without tightness.
