Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then restart the binding, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones dislodged, or similar, then treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you fear that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and leave it like this for a few days until circulation returns, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to pass for the patient, then do not release them until twenty days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Wherever it is around, then bind their hands to their neck, and let their necks be even, and guard against movement and agitation, and let them sleep on their back; know that this fracture will be healed in thirty or thirty-five days, perhaps even twenty, according to the compositions and the constitutions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	On the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and on the knuckles there are few fractures, but rather bendings often occur.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, it is necessary that the patient should lie on their side, and sit upright facing them evenly; then place their hand on a stretched cloth, and the ministers must extend the broken bones, setting them in line with each other until they are well-aligned; apply the plaster and bandages, unless abscesses appear, and then put a splint according to the size of the place; let it be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the front of the ankle, make a circle of cloth, and instruct the patient to tighten it onto their broken ankle; then take a long strip of cloth, and let the heart-shaped sole be as big as the palm of your hand, and tie it tightly, just as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must place a sole above and another below the ankle, so that the feet are open and straight, then bind everything around the foot, and stop the bandage between the toes.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our toes, be it the big toe, place it evenly as needed; and bind it with the foot, and if you wish to put a small straight sole to raise the fracture, and prevent movement; and if the fracture is on other toes, like the index or one of the others, treat them equally, and bind them with the next healthy toe; either bind them all together in an 'I' shape, which is better, or place above a sole as for the big toe; and take care during the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, help those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken thigh.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it can be easily seen when the limb turns forward or backward; its restoration lies in binding a splint above and another below the break.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on their face, then each assistant stretches out their ligature to an equal portion of the limb; this is when the break occurs in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the break is near the hip joint, one of the splints should be towards the wrist and the other below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If the break is close to the knee joint, then the splint should be placed alongside the knee and its extension below; thereafter, have two assistants grasp the bone with both hands in its natural alignment before applying a plaster cast and bandaging it tight so as to avoid abscesses forming later on.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down before you return to your work and treatment; the procedure is carried out in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap the fracture with I hard bandage doubled in II or III, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the groin, and pass I long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread above; then return the bandage over the leg and the thigh, then place stars on the fracture, and put a star on the bone of the leg; then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the tightening even, then start tying strongly III turns or IV above the fracture; and as you go up past the fracture, tighten it less; then take hold of II ends of the thread that you have passed between the leg and the thigh, and tie III stars that are on top, then return below at the end of the thread, until you come near the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, so that there is no abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, then release it and address what comes next, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of bone that catch, you must remove them if possible; and if not, then the site must be split open and pulled apart; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	In some cases, the thigh is fractured and treated with splints, like in the shoulder or arm; however, despite this restoration being done properly, the patient still feels discomfort.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the thigh is restored in approximately 50 days, or a little less or more, depending on the variety of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is little breakage in the knee joint, but it bends often.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is but a crack or an opening, and this happens with all wounds, both felt and unseen, causing great discomfort.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is achieved by placing what is round evenly on both sides until it is assembled as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and insert a round rod if needed, securing it accordingly, then follow all steps we have mentioned for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar cases; provide each accident with its appropriate treatment until healing occurs.
de la brisure de la jambe	On fracture of the leg,
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightly named 'shinbone', and the other is called 'calf'; they both have similar fractures as those occurring in the arm, and therefore their restoration equals that of an arm's bone fracture, with identical procedures involved. If the two bones break together, it leads to a leg-wide torsion.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bone is broken, it twists forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one experiences severe pain, which is easily noticeable; it twists below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then provide traction and align it equally, and bind the splints evenly; however, if the fracture is severe with multiple fragments, make the traction less intense and more gentle; adjust as per your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, and le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, no fracture occurs; fractures of the bones of the foot and toes are common and can be found in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a fracture of the foot bones and you see these bones overlapping each other, have the patient place their foot on the ground, as if they were about to walk; then put your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, press them until they return to their places; then apply a poultice and dress it, placing underneath the belly of the foot a small board with two curved ends, then secure it to the foot appropriately, wrap it all around with bandages and other materials you may need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equalized, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any fingers broken, reset them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a peg in the broken finger according to its length, and slightly wider, then put beneath it that board I mentioned, and strain it appropriately; if there are two or three, or more, broken, so place on each finger a peg according to its size, wrapped in a piece of linen cloth, and secure the board beneath the foot; and let it extend over the head of the board from outside the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I mentioned for other fractures, just like we have said; and help each accident as it is required.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone in the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's pelvis is fractured, make her sit with legs spread apart, then lean towards her back part and be held from behind; fill the vagina opening, which is nature-made for the patient, with cotton as big as your thumb; get the woman stand up and lift her spine slowly and gradually and the bone will come out along with the stool; when she wants to urinate take away the cotton, but put it back after that. Do this process seven days or so: this fracture would be cured and if you want do another trick as follows: make a goat's bladder attached to one end of a tube at the vaginal opening then blow through the other end with all your might until the bladder swells up inside; the vagina will be restored back, fill it again with cotton and let it stay there for some days till healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from one who puts his study and use into it, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates to many its proper path of restoration; understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert it into the penis; then wrap cloth around it, and leave for three days thereabout, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	If the fracture is accompanied by a wound, take a clean bone from an animal that died naturally and has not been slaughtered; then break this bone to fit into the hole of the broken one, and fix it in place with wax. Apply hot oil on the outside and keep the patient warm for three days, and he will recover swiftly.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with an open wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, that he be bled now, so that the bleedings we have mentioned may bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, apply some vitriol to it; and if you have nothing else, begin again to restore the fracture that very hour or day, so that no abscesses come of it.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does come of it, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, so that the abscess may subside; and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible through uncovered skin, you must set it gently with your hands in small movements.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not equipped to align with your hands, use this instrument made of iron which has VII or VIII doits in length and its width depends on the size of the wound; it's necessary for the surgeon to grip III or IV, depending on what is needed for each bone fracture treatment. It should be round and a little thick so that it doesn't bend when compressed against the limb during your work and sharp at one end with a wide base leading forward like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	It is called a "palainche", so it's important that the curved heads are placed on top of the exposed bone, push it in one swift motion until it returns to its place and make sure they're aligned with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone properly, you must cut away some of the head of the bone until the instruments have a better grip on it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, either a cutter or a saw, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small bark-like pieces.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is realigned, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not yet in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Do this until it is in its correct position, then moisten a cloth with black styptic wine and apply it properly to the area if appropriate; do not place any ointment or other greasy substance on the wound as this will cause it to fester and corrupt; afterward, administer stars when you have restored the bone, leaving the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around according to the size of the wound, taking great care that the wound is not constricted by the break; many times foolish surgeons have done this, causing their patient either death or corrosion in some cases; and be aware that these constrictions are softer and gentler than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is severe or large, and you fear bad accidents may occur as we have mentioned, and you find pain at the site, then do not place needles on it; instead, wrap it tightly with hard bandages, and tie them securely.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is becoming inflamed, remove what you have placed on it entirely, and apply healing ointment to it, such as four-herb ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must stretch the limb twice daily, in the morning and at night, until it is firmly attached and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be supported in such a way that the inflammation flows downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many die, and it cannot heal but returns crooked, know that there are small bone fragments, which is why you must search the wound thoroughly, and remove all those loose fragments that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms in that place, or any other kind of corruption occurs, you must treat it according to what he states in the aforementioned chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and protruding from the limb, such as the thighbone or shoulder blade, and other similar large bones, do not extract it, for many times this leads to death. Leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out on its own after twenty or thirty days. Then treat the wound if you can; otherwise, leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Wounds that come above the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of fractures, especially when it is close to the joint, and it is an ugly sight for the appearance of the limb; and sometimes the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if it is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, galbanum, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with a styptic wine or with egg white glue or with soap; put it on the night in swabs, holding it tight, and do not release by hand for several days; then remove it, and start another one until the nodations are removed; you can also restrain it over a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from members; if the nodation has already hardened like stone, and must be removed, so cut above it, and open the superfluity present; or shave it with a razor until it is removed, then treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the member which is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the broken bone is set and afterward the limb remains weak and feeble, this occurs for many reasons: one being that it was bound too tightly and wasn't tied as it ought to have been; or because there were too many ties and nourishment couldn't reach the limb; or due to excessive leeching; or from too much movement, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in their body, thus they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you must make the patient eat and soften their body so that blood multiplies within them; bathe them and provide joy and comfort; then apply ointment to the limb such that the ointment attracts great nourishment, frequently bathing it with warm water until the nourishment reaches the limb; and return it to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of a limb twisted after injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the broken bones are clearly visible, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken again completely, and many a fool has done this in our land; these procedures are condemned and cause great harm, even death; however, if the swelling and pain are fresh, they should be treated with hot water, or softening herbs that have been cooked, such as leaves of mallow, roots, marshmallow root, and similar things; then apply a softening plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster out of it; alternatively, you can take fatty figs, grind them with bran of wheat, and other medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And at times, the swelling is reduced by constantly and for a long time rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And provide gentle movements to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting and hardening is like stone, and it needs to be removed with an iron tool, then you must cut down to the bone, using a delicate and light incision device; and apply cauterization and give careful attention to its treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, you must now reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If you delay, the joint will swell, and it may be set back in place painfully; therefore, one must not move it when it is swollen: many times this causes abscesses and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave them alone until the abscess subsides; afterward immerse the limb in warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the cure becomes evident.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered chapters on dislocations of the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and perfect, you must reset it quickly without delay; in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and pushes one of their hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation involves two parts; and the other hand should be outside to provide balance; instruct the patient to loosen their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the practitioner places it evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if both jaws are involved, bathe them in warm water and oil until they can be gently moved back into place; do not delay the resetting process as we have stated.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into place evenly, and the patient's wound is well closed without softening, apply wet compresses made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on their back, with their shoulders supported by two pillows, so that they do not move them to the right or left, nor strain themselves trying to eat, but take light food until the pains are gone, and the jawbones are relaxed; thereafter chew what you wish lightly, and make no effort to open your mouth widely when eating or drinking, until the jawbone is well healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset at once and are not restored to their places, then fever and customary flux will result, possibly a discharge of the belly, perhaps vomiting pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and many times the one who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	From a fork or cleft.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from the side within its structure and is rarely dislocated externally; one can feel this well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on their back and stretches out their arms; then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply a plaster and bind it, and hold it in place; and the head which faces the cut cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it dislocates again, then reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage, and hold it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; similarly, the shoulder head is restored when it is displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder dislocation occurs in three ways: first, it dislocates at the lower part of the socket; secondly, at the back part; and occasionally, it dislocates upwardly, which is rare; it never dislocates backward or inward towards nerves. It often dislocates downwards toward the socket, especially in those with less fat because it easily slips out; for those with sufficient fat, it barely dislocates and returns barely.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And occasionally it happens to some men that they suffer from a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells due to a hot abscess, and they believe it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is recognized as dislocation when it falls towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find an obvious disparity between them; and at the head of the shoulder, you will see a hollow, and below the armpit on top of the shoulder joint, like an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose nor move in any way; and if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can feel it clearly upon touching; and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is recent or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the assistants lift the patient's hand upwards, then place your palms underneath the shoulder blade, and raise the joint forcefully to its proper position; the assistants lift the hand and extend it upward before placing it beneath the arm pit again; this will cause readjustment.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come about as we have said with hands outstretched afterward, then the patient must be bathed in warm water; and the assistants should apply a softening and soothing ointment such as a decoction of altee, fenugreek, and mellilot in water, which is to be administered; then the patient should be remembered on their back, and place underneath the shoulder blade an equal piece of woolen cloth, neither too soft nor too hard; then let the assistants place one's heel on the cloth and lift the shoulder with care, pulling the patient's hand; while another assistant holds the head steady so it does not move downwards. This will reset the shoulder immediately, and if you wish to proceed in this way: ensure that there is a man present who is larger than the patient; they should stand upright beside them and push their shoulder underneath the patient's armpit, then raise the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs from the air; another assistant pulls the patient's hand downward towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, you can place something heavy on them, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one resets it also in another manner: take a long stake and fix it in the ground so that its head is as level as possible with the shoulder; let it not be too thick nor too thin; then place the patient on top of it, but cover them with soft material first and let the arm of the affected side hang down along the length of the stake; then stretch out their hand downwards from the other side very carefully, so that the joint is gently eased back into its original position. If after all this the dislocation will not go in again, one may try this operation: take a stake two yards long and four inches thick at the head, which has a rounded end for insertion deep down under the shoulder blade; follow this procedure:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of the wounded man a soft cloth so that the wood does not hurt him; then put it under the sick person's armpit; and extend his arm along the length of the log, and bind the shoulder to the log, and the arm at the head of the hand; then place the arm on one step of a ladder with the wide side down, and let the hands be extended downward, and leave the body hanging on the other side: now the joint will come back in place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is there, in whatever way, you must put under the armpit a round pad of equal wool; then apply the plaster prepared with flour powder, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around, then strap underneath the armpit appropriately, and turn the bandage back onto the plaster, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hands stay like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he must eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster; then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; if it remains firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has entered it or for any other reason, you must apply cautery at three points as described before in the chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either severed or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be properly reset.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the armpit and breasts or behind is caused by a push or pull of hands and should be treated elsewhere; treat it until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing process, there is cracking in the limb and delayed movement, let the patient bathe frequently until this cracking is alleviated and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of shoulder dislocation:
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is repeatedly dislocated and returns with difficulty; if it's dislocated from all sides, especially front and back, and the dislocation isn't reduced properly because it's visible and felt; this varies according to each person.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person's wound with healthy flesh, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm or reach their shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before any abscesses form, because if abscesses appear, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when the dislocation is at the back; this is worse than other dislocations, causing even greater pain, and possibly leading to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows, when it can be reset, extend their arm with both your hands; spread their arms out, and hold their wrists according to where the cut is above and below, then push the joint back into its socket or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it occurs when one's hand doubles over their own hand, and you should fix this by firmly grasping the root of the palm where it has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not want to return to its place, perform a strong extension; with one minister extending the arm and another pulling it, so that it is not moved during this extension; then turn the arm from side to side, after you have wrapped around a thick piece of cloth which is long and wide; and when the physicians join the joint back together at their hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push on the joint firmly until it returns; once it is in place, apply dry plaster along with egg white, straining it tightly, and tie the arm up close to the patient's neck, leave them this way for a few days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, untie the bandage and let it be; but if you see that the joint does not heal properly, reapply the poultice and bandage, and leave it for a few days until it is securely set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels soreness after the joint is reset, and it changes, bathe and gently rub him, and press until it is soothed; or place over the joint a dressing of greasy sheep's wool, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and put him in a bath; when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then apply the dressing again, and put him back into the bath; do this two or three times until it is healed; if you wish, apply warm moist cow manure mixed with butter, and strap it on; he will return to his normal state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The knuckles of the hand dislocate easily, and they return lightly more than other joints. However, it is necessary to relocate them to their place immediately, in that very hour that they are dislocated, unless the place is swollen or an abscess appears there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the relocation is such that you place the afflicted hand on a table, and have the assistants stretch out the hand, and arrange it so it is even, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns. However, one must look to see if it is in its right place; then let the patient put the back of their hand on a table for extension and relocation.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place their palm-side down on a table and let the physician place his/her hand over the affected joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it dislocates again now, then it is well. If not, apply soothing emollients for hot abscesses and leave them there without reapplying.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if they cannot bear it and you are unable to relocate the joint after several days, then leave the joint deformed. It does not harm them while their hand is numb, preventing them from grasping anything; therefore know that either nerves or arteries have been severed. There exists no other mechanism beyond cauterization near this case, nor any other remedy worth pursuing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we mentioned above, then strain it and let it sit for five days; then unwrap and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move properly, and there is no crack or wound, then bathe it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand dislocate in every direction, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the inside; then extend the finger and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns to its proper place, then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the side where it is dislocated; leave it there for two days, and then straighten it that day; at night bind it as we have said, and unwrap it by day, make it move, and rewrap it at night; do this often until it is secure. And also do all of these steps if it is dislocated on the inside of the hand, and act in a similar manner to what you did before, until it is healed; and also do likewise when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of dislocation of the spine from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine from the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure for it, as death swiftly comes to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that gas escapes uncontrollably, and they cannot hold it in, and often certain limbs go limp, be it both thighs or arms, or at four places; this curvature which goes to the back is called "gilbositez": its cure is that you must turn if gilbositez came from childhood: there is neither a cure nor full recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or blows or similar things, the old ways of cure had many words but little benefit overall; I have shortened them according to my intent and made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the humpback condition that occurs on the chest in front, no one knows of its cure; and also for that which directly affects both sides, and only the one that specifically comes at the back can be cured, as I said; it is necessary that the patient lies extended face-down in a level place, and has padding beneath them so they do not harm themselves; then stick one iron rod into the head firmly in the ground, and another by the feet, tying a cord over the shoulders of the patient, and another at the hips, knees, and ankles; two assistants should hold these cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, each between the two rods; these must be very secure, both the rod as we have said and the assistant's hands pressing on the spine with their palms until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a board of three arm lengths long, place it beneath the wall, and let the patient lie on their side. Push the head of the board under the wall, then put the middle of the board over the spine; have the surgeons place their feet on the other end of the board, pressing hard until it returns to its place. If you wish, do it with a turning stick that turns toward the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Drive two stakes into the patient's head one arm length apart, and towards their feet insert two more, with each stake separated by a span of about an inch in every direction; have a hole bored through each stake where the turning stick passes, and let these be firmly planted so as not to move. Between each pair of such stakes place another single turning stake above which sit two smaller stakes one span long used to turn said stick; then bind that binding-string from among the axle to this turning stick near the head and likewise attach the other string around the feet to the opposite turning stick, wherein every assistant turns his stick through the whole length of said cord while the master adjusts the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is equalized, apply a desiccative plaster with an abundance of egg white, then place some cotton wool, followed by a wooden strip three fingers long to support the area where hunchbackness occurs and the part of the spine that remains healthy; bind this with a bandage as we have described, and let the patient take nutritious food until he is healed. Should anything happen at the end of his recovery, administer softening and soothing medicines along with the wooden strip we mentioned earlier. Sometimes an area behind the last vertebra in the back swells up, resembling dislocation; but this is a bone that has pushed through so there should be no concern because it may lead to death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; 
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of its dislocation is as follows: when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it will be longer, and the sick person's knee will appear more prominent than the healthy one; they cannot bend their knee properly, and the area nearby is swollen with a hot abscess due to the thigh bone being out of place.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign for someone who has recovered is as follows: this improvement is contrary to what was mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs for someone who has not recovered yet are as follows: they stretch their leg according to its length; however, bending the knee causes pain, and if asked to walk, they cannot do it properly, and they retain urine, with swollen testicles, and when defecating, they have to support themselves on their heels.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one who experiences this behind them are that they cannot extend their knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, the tendons are softened, and the head of the thigh bone is in place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	We treat this type of recurring dislocation by resetting it if the dislocation is old and remains in its position without any treatment; there should be no assumption made about its severity.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In the case of a fresh dislocation, there are four types of dislocation, so hasten to return the joint and stretch it inside and out, moving it right and left; perhaps it will go back, needing no other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong helper and grasp the leg firmly with both hands, or use a ligature tied above the knee; another assistant should place their hand over his shoulders, pushing their hands under his armpits, then bind him with a soft ligature around the thigh; another holds the head of the ligature; and all together they pull upward and downward at once, lifting the patient off the ground in one swift motion, leaving them suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must treat it in the following way: when the dislocation is to the outside, place the patient on their healthy side and apply a ligature above the root of the thigh and below the joint; another assistant should grasp his arms and embrace the affected limb firmly from behind, then extend forcefully outward: this will return it to its socket now; and this type of dislocation is less severe than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in this manner that we have described, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft bandage over the heels and knees, with the diseased leg extended twice as much as the other; then suspend him from the head of a pole, so that he is about two arm's lengths above the ground; then instruct one attendant to embrace the head of the thigh, while another attendant hangs alongside the patient, firmly embracing the thigh, because now the joint will quickly come back into place.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down as we have said for one with curvature, and bind his healthy leg tightly, and also his foot; then place two rods, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a rod between the thighs of the patient through a slit; and have moistened cloths planted around it so that they do not hurt the patient, then stretch each attendant towards him, and let the surgeon place himself level with his hand where the dislocation is.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a board, i.e., a table, and press as we have described for the hernia, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the affected leg until it hurts, and according to what I have said; place your weight on the healthy side of the patient's body, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	If the dislocation is on the outside, it should not be stretched downwards or lifted off the ground, but rather, it should be positioned as if the hip were dislocated outwards, just as we have described for lying down on both hips; let them lie on their face, and apply the binding as we mentioned earlier, and press on the joint with a board; when the patient can stretch their legs out evenly, and they are aligned, adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster, and strap it up with a bandage so that the hip does not move; let them rest for three or four days, then loosen the binding, and put the plaster back on; if you see that the legs remain equal in length, then bind as before, and leave it for another three days; afterwards, release the binding, and have the patient walk gently until their limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of knee dislocation.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees are dislocated in three ways: namely, inwardly and outwardly, and behind; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg towards their thigh, and if it does not reach their thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch their leg if they can, and place your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and push between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee sharply; and another assistant stretches their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it easily reaches their thigh lightly; and apply a plaster cast on it, and make the leg rest against the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then release it; and do not allow the patient to walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not broken, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	Sometimes the heels are bruised, sometimes fully dislocated, inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and more so on the part where it is dislocated: the resetting is light, and one must gently stretch it with their hands when it is only bruised.
